O, my children, now that I have completed this book, which is the last of the sciences of medicine, by the completion of its contents and by the exposition of it and by the clarification of it, in my view I have complicated for you to love this treatise, which is part of what I do with my hands, which is surgery.
For the operation with my hands has been abandoned in our region and in our time is entirely deprived, except that barely the science of it remains visible; and there are no more than a few small descriptions of it in the books of the Ancients, which have changed many things to errors and hesitation among those who understand it, weakening its force and the art.
And it is clear to me that I should revive this treatise according to the method of exposition and explanation and abbreviation; and so that it comes with the forms of cautery tools and other instruments used in the work as mentioned by adding explanation and preparation, which cause is necessary.
But the reason why a good craftsman is not found with his hands in our time is that the art of medicine is extensive, and one must be trained in the science of anatomy, which reveals knowledge of the functions of the members and their forms, as well as their connections and separations; and understanding of the bones, nerves, and muscles, their number and extension; and of the pulsating veins and stationary ones, and the places where they are found.
And for this reason Hippocrates said that in name there is much, but in the work little, and especially in the art of the hand.
This is what we have already said at the beginning of this book; for whoever does not know what we have said about anatomy cannot be excused from falling into error by which men are killed, as I have seen too many of them, for some are formed in this science and get themselves out of that lack of knowledge and experience.
For I saw a foolish and inexperienced doctor who had to incise an abscess in the neck of a woman, and he cut some arteries in the neck so that much blood flowed out, and the woman died as a result.
And I saw another doctor who claimed that he would remove a stone from a man who had been suffering from it, and the stone was large. When he came to do it, he pulled out that stone along with part of the bladder, so that on the third day the man died.
And I had already concluded that it was impossible to remove that stone, and I saw that because of the size of the stone and the condition of the patient, I knew for certain that he would die.
And I saw another doctor who was paid wages by a duke of our land to perform surgery, and he attended to a black castrated man who had a fracture in his skull. Because of the doctor's ignorance, he exposed the fracture over the wound with cotton and splints in a strong structure but did not leave room for drainage.
And he loosened it according to his desires, and soon after he dressed the wound again. He then left it like that for several days and commanded us to remove the bandage; and thus it was that the skull and the flesh became abscessed, and he came to ruin.
Thus he calls to him, and prepares to loosen the bandages, and when calm is achieved he begins to relieve his pains.
But when corruption was confirmed in the member, because he could not restrain it, and it did not cease to spread the corruption within the member until the patient was in danger.
And I saw another surgeon who punctured a cancerous abscess, and it became ulcerated after some days, until the magnitude of its wickedness was evident to him, the lord of it.
The reason is that the melancholic humor in cancer is pure, therefore it does not need to reach every part of the body entirely, but rather remains in the member which suffers from being wholly affected by it.
And for this reason, my children, it is necessary for you that the operation be planned in two aspects: one is an operation associated with health, and the other is work where there is risk even in the best conditions.
And I have already mentioned this in every place in this book where an operation occurs with error and fear; therefore, it is necessary for you to keep this in mind and avoid that, so that the pages do not find a way to speak ill of you and dishonor you.
And so take up your arms with diligence and the protection of God, and your patients with skill and firmness.
And use the best path by God's grace to lead to health and praiseworthy success, and leave behind the terrible diseases that are hard to cure, and stand firm against what makes you fear, so that hesitation in your faith and reputation does not escape you: for it remains more to your glory, and even more in this world and forever in your sanctity.
Wound treatment in some monastic surgeries: Do not treat illness badly, for then bad doctors are not named.
And thus I have dedicated this book in three parts.

I shall speak of the quality of the movements of that cautery and of its ingredients, and in what condition cauterization is prohibited.
Therefore, I say that the speech about the quality of the movements of cauterization and its ingredients is long and verbose, subtle by science, and hidden as a secret; many wise people have spoken much about it, and they are often at odds with each other. For me, a little of their speeches suffices to avoid prolongation.
And so I say that cauteries conform to all complete structures universally, whether they are made of material or without material, with the exception of two structures, which are tail-like structures without material.
In the dry and material-tail structure, they become dehydrated; for some say that cauterization is beneficial for this, while others say the opposite, that cauterization is not appropriate in a disease characterized by quality and dryness, because the nature of fire is hot and dry, and it is inappropriate to treat a tail-like and dry condition with something as hot and dry.
And he who says the opposite of that is wrong, because cauterization can be beneficial in all tail-like and dry diseases that occur in human bodies, for when you compare the condition of a person's body and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find that the human body is cold and moist.
And I say with the words of that person, that I have already discovered this through some experiences myself.
But I do not mean that one should rely solely on what has already been expounded and exercised in the chapter of cauterization through previous practice, without knowing the diversity of human structures and the disposition of diseases in their seasons, and the causes of those diseases, as well as their symptoms and the time span involved.
But in other structures, there is no need for fear, especially in cold and humid diseases, because all doctors are now in agreement about those, and they do not disagree on the benefit of using cauterization in such cases.
And know, my children, that the secret of healing through cauterization with fire and its goodness lies in the fact that fire is simple, and its action affects only the member being cauterized without harming other parts of the body except for minor damage.
Here is the translation:
May the fire, by its exalted nature and goodness of substance, do nothing but cause superfluities to overflow. And it is known to us through experience and length of service in studying this art concerning the truth of causes; and for that reason I excuse myself from the length of speech. And if not that it would not be read in my book, at this place I hide from you secrets about the fire, and its quality in operation on bodies and expulsion thereof by which you expel diseases, with a philosophical demonstrative speech, which would sharpen your wits.
And know, children, that those who disagree about the time when it is convenient to perform cauteries pause at the best time of spring.
And I say that cauteries are convenient at all times, because the harm caused by accidental circumstances of time is submerged in the benefit brought about by what is attracted through cauterization, and even more so if the cautery is for pains or necessary pain, strength and swellings, which cannot tolerate delay due to fear of malice, which is worse than a small harm entering through the time.
And this does not concern your understanding, or, children, what is valued only by the common people and foolish doctors is that for the disease which is cured by cauteries there is no delay at all times, and they pause at that consequence.
And the reason is not thus as they think, because cauteries are nothing but a replacement for medicine that alters the complexion and dries up the humidities which are the cause of pains.
But may it be that superfluous cauteries are above medicine due to the speed of their validity and the virtue of their operation and the greatness of their power.
It is possible that his illness may return at some time according to the condition of the patient and the location of his illness, and its nature, and what has been prepared in him by the accumulation of superfluities within him, and what he has acquired through food and similar causes; but if the illness for which cautery was administered is a subtle one involving few superfluities and humidities, such as dental cautery for pain and the like, it may not return, though this applies to minor cases.
And the common saying is that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, and it is said by practitioners, not because those who understand it think it to be a cure beneficial to medicine or any other cause before applying cautery.
And the cause is contrary to that; and the understanding that cautery is the last remedy of medicine is only when we administer methods of cure for certain illnesses, and those remedies do not suffice, and then at the end of the treatment, cautery is administered, and it proves effective. And here in what follows, I mean that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, not according to the understanding which the common people and foolish doctors have.
And the ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and they did not say this except for the equality of gold and the excellence of its substance.
And they said that the location for cautery does not matter, which is not absolutely true, because I have already experienced and proved that it works differently on different bodies; cautery with gold can be good and better than iron as others claim. However, when you perform cautery using fire with gold, it is not clearly defined to you, because the hardness of gold requires careful adjustment regarding quantity, and it prepares to receive friction. If you apply heat over it by fire, the gold will melt due to the heat, and if you place some thin sheets in the fire, the craftsman can perform the cautery according to that condition.
And thus is made the cautery of iron, which must be applied gently and gradually in accordance with the correctness of the procedure.
And I have arranged this chapter on cauteries according to the chapters, and I have placed those of the head among the parts, so that I alleviate the questioning of him who seeks what he desires.
The first chapter.
This cautery is applied to the headache caused by cold and moisture, which are the two causes of such an accidental condition. It is also used for a profuse running sore called "corissa" in the head, cheeks, and ears, excessive sleepiness, toothache, gout, and generally all illnesses that arise from coldness, such as paralysis, stroke, and similar conditions.
The method of this cautery is as follows: First, command the patient to evacuate their bowels with a laxative medicine for three or four nights, according to the strength of the patient and their age and usual habits.
And then command him to shave his head with a razor, and then have him sit between two chairs and place his hands on his own feet.
And then place the palm of your hand on the shaved part of the head near the bridge of the nose between the eyebrows. But when the heat of your hand has reached that place, mark it with ink, and then prepare the olive wood cautery, which is made as follows:
And so pause there about the marked spot until it descends, in such a way that the skin may be gradually stretched, and you turn it.
And then lift your hand gently and look at the spot, and if you see any amount of bone already exposed, like the quantity of grain in a thimble, then raise your hand, and if not turn your hand to that tool, another of those, if it is chilled, until you can see the bone which I have told you about.
And then take a little salt and dissolve it over the spot and let that remain for three days.
And then pause over the embedded wound on the border and let that remain inside until the burn scar is destroyed. And then treat the spot with a four-component ointment until it is healed.
And they say that when the plague boils burst open, it is better and more beneficial to let them drain.
And some of them say that the cord should be cauterized down to the bone, and the cautery should remain until it adheres to some part of the bone.
And then remove what is adhered to the bone, and then treat it.
And others say that with the cautery it should reach the deepest part, until it presses strongly into the bone until the bone melts, and this is the way to cauterize slightly: And they believe that from that spot emanates the vapor of the head.
And let the wound be treated for some time until it is healed and consolidated.
But I have not seen these two species of cautery used universally, but only on certain individuals out of fear; and leave that, in my opinion, it is better to heal with care, when possible; for the head is delicate due to the solution of continuity as we have testified regarding other members, and especially when the patient's constitution is cold.
And the first species of cautery is safer and better, in my opinion; and with that, one can heal and bring about health.
Chapter Second.
Of cauterizing the head.
When chronic and long-lasting pain occurs throughout the head and this is prolonged in the patient, and if you have used plasters, compresses, decoctions, poultices, ointments, cataplasms, and various other remedies, especially if it has already been cauterized with one cautery which I mentioned but to no avail due to any of those causes, then consider whether the patient's head is strong in its constitution; and if it is not cold and does not have much moisture, then at that time cauterize with another type of cautery below that one a little. And then cauterize that area above the crown of their head with cautery until the pain is relieved. Cut open the pain and expose the amount of bone that we have described and cauterize that area with a cautery at the back of the head in the place called "vas" — which is the location where the vein is situated. And take care in this, and do not expose the bone, for the patient will thereby discover great pain different from the pain of all other cauteries of the head.
And I will describe this cautery in its place, for it is appropriate that the cautery with which you cauterize the horns of the head and the occiput is a finer cautery than that with which the middle part of the head is cauterized; and this is the form of it.
Chapter Three.
On Cauterization of Non-Ancient Hemorrhoids.
When severe pain occurs in the part of the head, or if there is persistent pain inside the eye, one should evacuate with medicines that purify the head, and administer the other treatment which I have described for diseases; and if this does not benefit, then cauterization should be performed in two ways: either with a sharp medicinal cautery or with iron.
But if you are performing a cautery with a burning medicine, then take a piece of cloth, soak it in the medication, and hold its extremities from both ends. And then cut into the area of the pain on the temple with a lancet slightly so that it is done in a hidden place, where it is concealed.
And then apply pressure to it with bandages by tightening them properly, and leave it like that for three hours; then loosen the bandages and remove the cloth, and leave the wound open for two or three days, and then place a poultice over it soaked in butter until the area becomes warm.
Let the treatment be applied until it is healed.
And if you wish, use some of the medicines mentioned in the twelfth chapter on burning medicines.
But when you apply cauterization, do it in this manner: prepare the cautery fire, of which this is the form:
and it is called a nail clamp, for its head has the shape of a nail with some curvature, and in the middle part there is a small protrusion.
And then apply it to the location of the pain, and hold your hand — so that the artery below is not adhered to — and move the tool gently little by little with speed.
And if the amount that adheres due to the stiffness of the tissue is such that it exceeds half of it, raise your hand so that the artery below is not adhered to, so that there is no flow of blood.
And then soak cotton in salt water and apply it to the location, and leave it for three days; and afterwards apply dry cotton around it, and treat with internal medications until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize at the end of the radial bone according to the cautery method, and be careful not to cut the artery in this proper but non-traditional procedure.

Place it on the area of pain along a line that is half the length of your finger or slightly more, and after placing your hand carefully, press firmly to ensure it does not cut the artery but reaches the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to guard against the continuity of the jawbone, which is malformed due to mastication, and that the lizard not adhere and the nerves which move it, and that it not become spasm.

Chapter VI.
On the cautery of the turtle.
The tumor which is cured without cauterization is nothing but of the kinds that come from phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases.

And pause your cauterization on the opposite side of the affected part, because softening occurs only in the part that appears healthy.
The method of cauterization is that you cauterize there with the cautery on the right side of the uppermost part of the ear, and a little above the horn of the head, and in another temple area, the length of which should be according to the length of your thumb, and then move your hand with the cautery until half the quantity of the tumor is burnt.

Chapter XVI.
Of cautery of the eyelid when the hairs turn inward and pain occurs.
When the eyelashes turn inward and cause pain, cautery can be performed in two ways: either by actual burning or by using a combustible medicine.
If the cautery is done with fire, instruct the patient to trim their eyelashes as one would for a normal haircut, ensuring they are lengthened and even; and if pain persists due to their growth, then wrap the eyes in a bandage so that nothing interferes until the lashes regrow.
When they have grown and are even, then instruct the patient to place their head in a comfortable position, and gently apply over the eyelid of the affected eye a mark resembling a leaf shape, with the beginning of the mark near the lashes.
And then place a cotton ball soaked in egg white or mucilage of fly wings on the eye.
And then perform the cautery according to this method.
And then cauterize gradually over the marked figure in small strokes until the surface of the area, which is like a myrtle leaf, is fully burned through.
And the sign of success in this procedure is that you see the eyelid of the eye becoming contracted and the lashes elevated away from the surface of the eye.
And then raise your hand and wash the area for three days, and afterward place a cotton ball on it until the scar is remedied. And for its treatment apply those plasters which will heal it.
If the hair returns because of some cause affecting it and the eyelid is softened, now make another attempt at cauterization over that area just as you did initially.
But if the hair grows on the eyelid below, now cauterize that area until it is raised to its natural position and healed so that the hair does not touch the eye.
But the cauterization and medicine should be such that you instruct the patient to pluck the hair until they are lengthened and healed, and then make from paper or cloth the shape of a myrtle leaf.
And then take known soap and one ounce of any living oil, and mix these ingredients well, and apply this quickly so that it does not dry; and then spread this over the paper made in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and place this on both eyes; and place under each eye cotton soaked in albumen, and have the patient's head in your lap.
And place your finger on the medication and press it gently so that the patient feels the burning of the medicine, for this burning is like that of fire.
And as long as the burning sensation persists, then remove the medicine and press it with your finger; when the burning stops, then rinse the eye with water; and now check if the eyelid is raised as it should be after rinsing, whether you need to treat it with fire or incision, for this indicates that it is well done; and if not, return the medicine to the place where it was not applied before it darkens until it heals your operation and contracts the eye.
Here is the translation:
It is necessary for you to guard your operation with vigilant diligence so that no part of the medicine falls into the eye, and if the eyelid after some days becomes softened and any cause of hair growth appears in the eye, then repeat your medicine upon that place where the eyelid has become softened, and properly as you did at the beginning, and soon it will be healed.
And this is the form of the myrtle leaf.
And you should know that the eyes of people vary in size and smallness, and therefore according to this is made your adjustment.
And the path to rectitude will not be hidden from one who studies in this art.
Chapter XVII.
On Cauterization of a Fistula That Is in the Lacrimal Sac of the Eye.
When you treat a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases and do not refer to your treatment, then it is necessary that you cauterize according to this method: instruct the patient to place his head in your lap, and hold the patient's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move or shake.
And then place a piece of cloth soaked in egg white or in a poultice of bran over the eye of the patient.
And then ignite the cautery, which has this form:
which is made of copper, similar in shape to a reed or an eagle's feather, with one end where the cautery is made.
And if you wish, insert it into the other extremity. And if you want it to come out like a probe.
But the one that is concave is better for the present purpose.
And then press the fistula if it is open, and let it drain and dry it out. And if it is not open, now cut it and extract the pus from it.
And then press on it with the cautery which should be well heated, and hold it there for a moment but do not bring the cautery too close to the eye, so that you do not accidentally burn your hand or cause harm, and now place the cautery on the flesh around the area and cauterize it.
And so if at the beginning of your cauterization it penetrates to the bone, that is good; and if not, then repeat the cauterization once or twice, as needed; and leave it like that for three days, and then press on the wound gently and around it apply a drying agent until it heals.
But if after these days it has not healed, then apply a sharp corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed and proceed as appropriate according to the relevant chapter.
And there is another method of cauterizing a fistula which the ancients first described: enter the location of the fistula and dilate it, and then place a thin cautery in that fissure whose form resembles the fistula: And pour into it one ounce of molten lead; and hold your hand gently but firmly, and do not move too much so that the molten lead does not reach the eye; and ensure that you press on the affected area gently, either in egg white or water, as the lead adheres to the location of the fistula and heals it miraculously.
And if the fistula is healed with what we have said about cauterization and treatment, that is well; but otherwise, it is necessary to administer traction of the nose and reduce the fistula to the body of the nose according to how it will come into its proper place.
Chapter XVIII.

Chapter XIX.
On Cauterization of Fistula in the Mouth.
When an abscess occurs in the uvula or on the palate or in the gums around the teeth, and then it becomes inflamed, and subsequently ruptures, and is neglected, and a fistula is formed, and when you treat this and the treatment does not succeed, then it is necessary for you to prepare a cautery according to the size of the fistula, and then place that heated cautery into the fistula, and hold your hand until the hot iron reaches the base of it, and do this once or twice; and then treat it with what we have said about treatment until it heals.
Therefore, if the sinew is cut and it heals, that is good; but otherwise, it is necessary to discover the place and remove the corrupted bone as will be explained in its chapter.
Chapter XX.
On cauterization of the teeth and softening of the gums.
When the gums have been softened by humidity and the teeth are dirty, then using those medicines and not conferring, place the tip of the cautery in its proper position, and immediately ignite it so that you place the tube over the tooth and quickly introduce the ignited cautery into it; keep it there for just a little while until the pain from the heat of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
Then remove your hand, and immediately repeat the cauterization several times as you wish.
Then have the patient rinse his mouth with salt water and hold it for one hour, after which he can spit it out, because the dirty tooth is cleaned and the softened gum is strengthened and the corrupted humidity is dried up.
Chapter XXI.
On cauterization of toothache.
When toothache is due to coldness, or there is decay or worm damage, and if you do not confer on the cure with medicine, then cauterization in such cases can be done in two ways: either by using a cow's horn or by using fire.
Cauterization with horn is when you take a cow's horn and boil it in vinegar, then take cotton and wrap it around the tip of the horn. Immediately immerse the boiled horn in hot oil, and quickly place it on the painful tooth until it is cooled by contact.
From there, apply some burnings until the heat of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you do, soak linen or cloth in the aforementioned broth, and place that on the aching tooth, and place hot iron over it until the heat of the iron reaches the pain around the tooth.
However, when using cautery with fire, you should attend to the thickness of the iron or metal, and it should be in the middle of some thickness so that the intensity of the heat does not reach the mouth of the patient.
And then apply the cautery with fire in the form that will come, and place it on the tooth and move it around until the cautery is rubbed; do this several times until the pain subsides either on that day or the next day.
And it is necessary that the patient gargle with good broth due to the application of the cautery and hold it in their mouth for one hour, then spit it out; this is the form of the cautery.
And cauterize as much as you wish according to what is possible for you.

Chapter XXVIII.
On the puncturing of an abscess of the kidney with a cautery.
When you find an inflammation or abscess in the kidney and wish to know whether that abscess is in the flesh of the kidney or in its capsule, if it is in the flesh of the kidney, the patient will experience heavy pain and acute discomfort.
And if it is in the capsule of the kidney, the pain will be intense and often weary the physicians with its treatment.
Therefore, have the patient lie on their back; and then feel the location of the abscess by touching it; and subsequently ignite the cautery which resembles a reed, the form of which was described in the previous page. And cauterize with that cautery until the entire tube is consumed, until it reaches the pouch, until it causes healing.
And then treat that area as you would for other abscesses until it is healed.
And it is not advisable to use this method of cautery except by one whose study in the art of medicine is extensive and who has knowledge of many diseases; but even then, after experimenting a few times with such an operation, it is better to leave it to more experienced hands, which is safer.

Chapter XXX.

And there is another method of cauterizing, which is to ignite the cauteries using two vertical lines, a cause we have mentioned in the chapter on the dislocation of muscles, and elevate the shoulder, which is on the right side of the boil where the weight of the wound falls on the left side.
And let your elevation be such that when you raise the shoulder according to the length of the body, the cauteries are made according to the width of the body.
And then insert the two vertical lines, ignite them immediately, in that area where they penetrate the opposite shoulder.
And then remove the cauteries; thus four cauteries are completed.
And if you want to cauterize, have three burnings prepared.
And if the wound from which you want to cauterize has been bandaged for too many days, because it may be more convenient than other previous causes in the treatment.

And let the patient lie on their back for forty days until the place is sealed and the plague subsides.
And it is necessary to suspend the patient's nutrition according to the length of time required for the cure, during which the intestines should not be damaged by excessive force in treating them.
And when you want to start removing it after forty days, administer it gradually and properly, and continue for another forty days.
And let them be reduced in work and in the intake of food and drink, and in loud speaking, for when they follow this regimen of complete recovery, they will be healed.
And I will describe the treatment of ruptures in other parts of the abdomen, and at the beginning, if you do not want them to spread, then cauterize the rupture with a round cautery according to its size; let this be removed as much as one-third of it from the cord; and subsequently treat it as we have said, and it will heal.
And some earlier practitioners said that the rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery in this form, as it is marked with a template:
This is a paused line that you follow through the latitude in the flesh above the rupture, and another line above it; then pause your hand with a cautery nail, but the first cautery is farther and better.
Chapter XLVI.
On Cauterization of Dislocations.
When you find in any members by falling or by striking pain that persists and the pain continues for a long time and does not improve with medicine, then it is necessary to cauterize with a pointed cautery.
And let the cautery for each member be according to its size and smallness, and its strength and delicacy, and the location of the dislocation and the pain in it.
If it heals with the first cautery, that is good; but if not, then repeat the cautery on it. For it is customary for such pains to be punctured in a member close to where the pain is, so you need to achieve this with the cautery until the patient is healed.
Chapter XLVII.
On Cauterization of Leprosy.
Some cases of leprosy are helped greatly by cautery, but rarely in the case of the type of leprosy that is caused by the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
And so when you want to cauterize that patient, consider whether the leprosy is widespread and has not been cured by what we have mentioned in the division and do not delay, and be afraid that the corruption will encompass the whole body of the patient and all its composition, then cauterize it on the head with v cauteries: one in the middle of the head, and the second further down, near the forehead at the end of the hair; and two on the temples; and one behind, on the nape or back of the neck.
And lastly your hand should apply the cautery a little inside where it presses on the bone, and from there the scars are displaced, so that the expulsion of thick vapors may be facilitated from there; and cauterize over the wound as is necessary.
And if leprosy has already spread over the body and is clearly manifest, then you should cauterize in those places with those cauteries which we have mentioned at the beginning; and one cautery on the tip of the nose, two cauteries on each cheek, two cauteries on two vertebrae of the neck, six cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, one large cautery on the vertebrae near the buttocks, one cautery on the buttocks, two cauteries on each thigh, one cautery on each ankle, two cauteries on each elbow and one on each wrist, two cauteries on each knee joint, two on each muscle, and two on each tendon of their feet; and cauterize that over all the joints of the fingers and toes, and on each heel of their feet, and on the hollows of their hands.
And be careful of the nerves which lie over the heel so that you do not burn those.
And in some cases it is cauterized with one cautery on the bone of the little toe and another on the mouth of the stomach, and another on the liver.
And know that the more you adjust the cauteries, the more beneficial and effective they are; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as others would, because his body is already numb.
And it is appropriate that the cauteries be large or few according to the members and joints as dictated by the properties of the tools.
Regarding the care of cautery, use flour of barley mixed with honey. For the other treatment, let it be for healing.
Chapter XLVIII.
On cauterization for stupor.
When a limb is numb or asleep and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and does not heal, then you should cauterize that numb limb with cautery according to the magnitude of the limb or the size of it.
And let the heat of the cautery enter slightly beneath the surface of the skin. And subsequently treat that area with an ointment so that it may heal.
And sometimes a cautery is applied to a numb area that extends to the ribs and spine, as well as to the points where the nerves that control that limb are located, and thus the numbness is alleviated.
But do not proceed with this unless one is wise in the anatomy of limbs and the distribution of nerves throughout the moving body.
Chapter XLIX.
On cauterization of ulcers that are infected.
When an old ulcer does not respond to any of the medicinal ointments, then you should cauterize it with cautery slightly according to the quantity and specificity of the skin so that the whiteness and color of it change, and its color be altered.
And subsequently treat that area with flour of barley and lentils mixed with rose oil and leaves of arnica, and either dove blood or swallow blood, using an equal part of each and mixing them all together, then apply a bandage over it so that it may heal.
Chapter I.
On cauterizing wounds.
When cancer begins and you want to remove it, then cauterize that part with a cauterizing instrument in the shape of a circle around it as it appears.
And the wise say that it should be cauterized with the last cautery in its proper place; but I have not seen this done, for I fear that it may become ulcerated, and I have seen this happen several times.
It is safer to cauterize around the wound in a circular manner as we have said, or with words like these.
Chapter II.
On cauterizing of burns.
When a burn is delayed in healing due to the excess of matter it contains, or because of the patient's condition, being old and weak, with little blood, or because of the time; then cauterize around the wound with small punctures using a cautery instrument; and afterward apply something that will hasten its healing.
But if you want to make a perforation with the cautery, then use a cautery of this shape; and place it in the proper location of the burn until it penetrates the tissue.
And if the cautery is applied in a place that is further away, so that the arm is not burdened; and then care for it until it heals.
Chapter XII.
On cautery with corrosives.
Corrosives are like a wandering corruption in the limb, which consumes it as fire devours dry wood.
Therefore, when you see the corrosive in a place that can tolerate cautery with fire, then you ignite and apply small cauterizations, and larger ones as is appropriate in the location where the corrosion is.
And proceed to cauterize it from all sides until you eradicate all the corrosion and leave no cause for its recurrence.
And then dress it for three days, and apply ointment three times a day on the cauterized areas until all the scars are healed and all corruption is eradicated.
And then treat it with substances that promote flesh growth.
But if after three days you see that healthy flesh is growing where there is no more corruption, that is good. But if not, then repeat the cautery on what remains in the corrupted areas.
And some corrosives are treated with sharp medicines, for these serve as an alternative to cautery. But cautery with fire is more effective quickly.
And I have already mentioned the treatment with sharp medicines in the division above, and so use that when you find it necessary.
Chapter 53.
On cautery of nails and other similar cases.
In many cases, when dealing with the divisions or parts of the foot that are diseased and are called clavus, which is a thick, ingrown condition affecting the foot; and cautery for this can be done in two ways, namely fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Fire cautery is when you ignite the cautery in the shape of a crescent, which is made of iron according to the quantity that contains the clavus from all parts, and it should be fine-edged.
And then place the ignited cautery on the clavus, and then rotate your hand with the cautery around the clavus until the cautery reaches the depth of the clavus. And leave that for three days until it begins to form scabs. And then apply a plaster made of crushed wild mallows with salt to it, and leave the plaster on it for one night, because that will eradicate it from its roots.
And then treat the area with a healing flesh-generating ointment until it is healed.
And if it does not convert, and many times this happens on the surface of the body, mainly in the hands and feet, then you should administer hot water cautery to them. This is done by taking a small tube made of iron or brass or crescent-shaped, and place it on the clavus; then pour a small amount of hot water into the tube, and hold your hand, rotating it with the pressure of your hand completely, so that the edge of the tube touches the root of the clavus; and the hot water will flow towards the root of the clavus. Wait for the disease to react slightly to the heat of the water for an hour, and then remove it, as the clavus with its roots will be eradicated.
And thus place one finger next to another until you cover all of them with your hand.
And carefully treat those pus spots until the roots of the nails have been eradicated with the help of these ointments, with which the flesh grows back.
Chapter LIII.
On the cautery for trembling.
When you find a tremor due to irritation of the nerves or from fever causing irritation, or from some similar cause, it is necessary that you cauterize it with four cauteries or five on the vertebrae of the back, between each vertebra with one cauterization; and at the ankles, and above the stomach, use an olive-shaped cauterization.
And the trembling of the patient subsides and hastens the recovery from the illness.
Chapter LIV.
On the cautery for accidental injuries to the body.
When the body is suddenly injured and pus-filled wounds appear, which are formed from thick, corrupted matter; therefore, at the beginning when they appear, it should be cauterized over the entire head of the fistula with a fine cautery made of myrtle wood, the end of which is extended to the fire; or with long eagle talons; or with a lens-shaped cautery.
And sometimes it is appropriate to cauterize at the beginning of its expulsion according to this method; and if it is not done, then the excess matter that causes these issues is disrupted, and thus they heal from them.
However, it is necessary that this be done appropriately for evacuation and phlebotomy.
Chapter LX.
On cauterization of blood flow due to accidental cutting of an artery.
If the flow of blood from an artery that has been cut is prolonged due to the condition that caused it in the first place, or due to the beginning of abscesses or cauterization of the limb, and similar situations, then it is difficult to remedy this.
When such an accident occurs, immediately place your finger over the opening of the artery, and press on it with enough strength to stop the flow of blood until you can secure this position so that no more blood escapes.
And then place the olive wood cauteries, both small and large, in the fire for a number of moments, and blow on them until they are ignited.
And then take one of those cauteries, either small or large depending on the location and condition in which the artery is ruptured, and apply it quickly after you have removed your finger, so that the blood flow is sealed and restrained.
And if the blood is expelled from the opening of the artery when you remove your finger and apply the cautery, then take another cautery quickly from those that are prepared in the fire, and continue to do this one after another until the blood flow is stopped.
And be careful not to burn the nerve that is here, and ensure that it does not cause other harm.
And know that when blood flows from an artery, it is not possible then to restrain the blood, especially when the artery is large, unless by one of four methods: either by cauterization as we have said, or by extraction, for when it is extracted, the extremities are burned and the blood is restrained, or it may be bound with a ligature or bandage made of strong material, or it may be placed upon medicines whose virtue is to restrain the blood; and they may be strengthened with a pillow and moderate constriction.
And let him who administers moderate constriction with bandages and by means of cloths or through the positioning of burning substances and similar methods not hurry but proceed slowly.
And if anyone is to act and there is no physician present or medicine available, then gently press the tip of the finger on the opening of that vein as we have said, and understand the great constriction inside so that the blood stops from flowing from the upper part of the wound, and on the artery do not rub; and over the artery sprinkle with very cold water until the blood is congealed and thickened; and then decide whether cauterization or medicine is necessary.
Of incision and perforation and ventouses and of phlebotomy and of wounds and their similarities.
We have already stated in the first chapter all diseases in which cautery with fire is appropriate and burning medicines, along with their occasions and causes, and the instruments necessary for the forms of cauterizations; and I have organized the chapters on the superiority of the head among other parts.
In this procedure in this chapter by that method, so that the patient may be praised for it, at the time concerning what they have asked.
And before I begin this, take note, son, that in this chapter it is by means of fear what is in the first chapter on cautery.
And for this reason, it is necessary to be in great caution, because in the operation which is in this chapter many cases of evacuation occur, whether it involves blood or pus that sustains life, due to the application on the vein or incision over the abscess or opening an exit or purging a plague or extracting a splinter or starting a lithotomy or similar procedures. And in all of those cases, accompany fear and trembling, and in the most severe of them, death.
And I warn you that upon you does not fall what is in the case of hesitation, for some cases depend on your methods regarding people with various diseases. And among them are some who become angry about their illness and die quickly because of the intensity of what they find regarding their illness, and due to the length of the illness, and this anger signifies death.
And among them is one who gives away their possessions and says, "I hope for health from this," while their actual illness is fatal.
And therefore, you should not consent to those who come to you with this manner; and your caution should be greater than your greed and rapacity; and do not assume any cause without proper certain knowledge that verifies what concerns you, and for which a commendable tradition exists.
For the treatment of all your patients, prognosis and indication of what is beneficial to their health are necessary, for in that lies help for you in acquiring fame and memory, praise and glory.
O, children, may God inspire your mind and not take from you direction and protection, for this is in His hands.
And I have ordered this chapter to be distinguished by chapters as it follows the chapter on cauteries, concerning the treatment of the head among other parts, so that you may find what you seek and need from this.
First Chapter.
On the treatment of water that is contained in the head of children.
Know that this illness often afflicts children shortly after birth when the nurse presses too hard on the child’s head.
And at times it happens for hidden causes that are not known.
But I have seen this illness only in children; and to all those whom I saw it brought death, and thus it seemed to me to be a fatal condition.
And I have seen a child whose head was filled with water, and the swelling of his head was so great that he could not move due to the size of his head, and before long the humidity increased until it caused death.
And this humidity is either aggregated between the brain and the bone, or it is aggregated below the bone on the brain.
For when the operation is to be performed and the moisture lies between the bone and the abscess and the abscess is small, at that time you should cut in the middle of the head an incision in length, and let the length of the incision extend by two fingers’ breadth where the moisture runs, and this is the form of the spatum:
And if the moisture is more increased and the abscess is larger, then there are here two incisions according to this manner:
And if the moisture is below the bone, the sign of this is that you see the sutures of the head covered on all sides and the water is squeezed when you press it with your hand at the surface but not inside, and it is not hidden from you. You should cut in the middle of the head with three incisions according to this manner:
and immediately the incision extracts all the moisture; and then dress the incisions with cloths and bandages; and then pour over it vinegar and oil from the fifth day, and then loosen the binding and treat the wound with lint and unguents, and bind the head with equality; and eat the food that is dry with little moisture until the member is strengthened and healed.
And there is another method of incision, which you should consider based on the size of the abscess and the collection of water, for sometimes it is more in the occipital region, or in the front part, or on the right side, or on the left; and therefore attend to the incision where the abscess appears and the accumulation of water, and do this according to what is best for you.
And observe that you do not cut the artery and stop the flow of blood, or the patient will suffer harm from that flow of blood and evacuation of humidity.
Chapter Second.
When I deal with certain abscesses or wounds on the hands or feet, and if it is old and not treated with medication, then the last resort treatment involves these two arteries.
And therefore, when you want to cut those that the patient raises their hand, first rub the area with a rough cloth so that the arteries become visible; then bind the patient's neck with a cloth; and then observe where the pulse is felt; the locations of each are near the ears, though they may be hidden in some people.
And then press on the artery with your thumb, and then cut each one with a sharp scalpel, cutting deeply enough to reach the bone, and do this along the length of the head.
And if you wish, insert the scalpel below the artery and cut it where it meets the upper parts.
And the length of the incision should be about two fingers wide, because when an artery is cut, the blood flows out in a pulsating manner, frequently gushing forth.
But if the artery does not appear clearly, then measure from the ear a distance of three fingers, and then press with your thumb to find it, and make an incision down to the bone.
In what must be poured out of the blood is the quantity of one ounce, and it is light in weight when poured from barley or wheat, and all this is according to the amount which appears of the strength of the patient and the fullness of the vein.
And then consider the inflammation, and if any cause of pus remains on the bone, now incise that so as not to become an abscess by cauterization.
And then strengthen the inflammation with poultices and bandages of linen cloth, and afterwards treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Chapter III.
On the extraction of veins which are on the temples.
When it happens that someone suffers from chronic or acute headache due to excessive moisture in the body and its quality in the veins of the temples, or if it is similar to these conditions, and treatment with medicinal methods does not provide relief, then we resort to bloodletting from the veins on the temples, or cauterization as we have shown.
And the method of the operation and extraction of those veins is that the patient shaves the hair which is on the temples; and understand the visible vein in the temple as it is shown to you by its pulse, and it is concealed only in a few people due to the intensity of friction.
And if it is concealed from you, then tie the patient's head with some cloth; and afterwards rub the area with a rough cloth or evaporate the area with hot water until the vein becomes clearly visible. And then you take the spatum, which has this form: And then you peel the membrane in such a way that you reach the artery; and then cut it where necessary to extract it from the parts until you remove it from the membrane and uncover the tunics beneath, which you leave intact from all sides.
But if the artery is delicate, then wrap it at its extremity with a ligature, and then cut away a part according to the amount by which the ends of it need to be lengthened or shortened, and there will be no bleeding, for if they are not cut back in this way, the blood will not flow properly.
And then remove about half an ounce to three ounces of blood.
And if the artery is large, then place it in two places with a double-thick thread of flax or long cords, and do not allow it to become putrid before the healing of the wound, so that there is no bleeding.
And then cut away the excess that is between two ligatures; and do this either at that hour or another time.
And if you wish, cauterize it with a cautery to the bone or use a knife-shaped cautery until the ends of it are severed, and this will serve as a substitute for that procedure.
And it is better to perform this work when the patient does not have a fever or has a heated constitution; for cautery is among those causes that help eliminate final humidity, and thus it is better to do so while the condition is favorable.
Regarding the extraction of arteries, ensure that the place is clean beforehand, and lay the patient on a prepared surface decently, and nearby have dry medicines ready to promote flesh growth and warm applications to aid in healing.
And if during the procedure blood begins to flow from the artery, then you should work to restrict that blood, either by cauterization or by filling the area with cotton and pressing firmly so as to constrict the blood. And if none of those methods are available to you, then press your hand on the area until the blood is constricted, and apply the site with water of extreme coldness until the pain subsides, and continue applying pressure as needed.
And the most important thing in extracting an artery is that you cauterize the vein with this cautery using two irons, after marking both places with ink, and then place some material on fire so that it reaches the bone and cuts the vein at two points, so that what is between these ends can be extended, since it has not been fully consolidated by this cautery.
And this is the form of the cautery:
And the sharpness of the two irons should be exemplary. However, if you use slightly less sharp irons than two, it is better, for if they are as sharp as two irons, they may approach too close to each other and cut the flesh too quickly.
Therefore, when there is some thickness in the area, maintain the heat of the fire and cut through the flesh gradually.
This work is better than any other work and more concise.
And let the spaces between two ribs be the quantity of the thickness of a finger.
Chapter four.
About the treatment of acute and acidic tears of the eyes.
When there are acidic tears, and the condition affects the veins that appear on top of the head, and if you do not find any cause for treatment with medicine in this case, often the face of the patient turns red, and a sensation as if ants were moving can be felt in their forehead, and the eyes due to this become extremely weakened, so much that even the hair around them is noticeable, and the eyelids are scorched by the sharpness of the tears. The ancient masters were very careful in the treatment of such conditions, and they did not consider this treatment a simple matter.
And it is that you command the patient to pluck out the hairs that are on their forehead, and then make three incisions evenly spaced according to the length of the forehead. And if the length of the incision is two fingers: one incision should be evenly spaced along the length of the nose in the middle of the forehead, and the second according to the length slightly towards the movement of the tears that flow from the tear duct, and the third on the other side.
And be careful not to cut into the arteries that are on both sides, and extend your hand along the continuation of both jaws. And if the space between each incision is the quantity of three fingers apart.
And if you have a piece of prepared sponge or dry cloth with which you squeeze out the blood.
And then insert the spatum between two sharp points, which has this form for the incision: which is from the part of the flaps into the second incision. Excise all the tissue that is between two incisions on the crest which is above the bone, and then make this median incision into the second incision. And then stretch this spatum and insert into the first incision another tool called a knife, sharp on one side and not sharp on the other.
And pause the sharp side on the flesh adjacent to the tissue, and the blunt side within the bone, and move it until you reach the median fissure, and divide all the vessels that descend from the head to the heels.
But ensure that the incision continues to appear on the tissue, and then make this in the median fissure into the other fissure.
And when the blood flow is equal in quantity, press the places from which the clotted blood has been collected.
And then place dry, aged wood shavings in each fissure, and sprinkle them with powder mixed in vinegar and oil and sweet wine, to prevent an abscess from forming.
And on the third day, loosen the bandage and administer a large infusion of hot water or decoction, and then treat with ointment made of basilicon in rose oil and other ingredients until the wounds are healed.
Chapter 4.
On the treatment of phlegm through catharsis and the expulsion of fluids from the inner parts of the head.
When there is a sudden and continuous urge for catharsis in someone, and the fluids from the patient are expelled in small quantities due to their weakness, and if the condition of their eyelids is ulcerated with hair loss, and there is acute pain and severe tension in the forehead, then you should understand from these symptoms that the matter and catharsis do not come except from the small veins of the inner parts.
And the best treatment for this is as follows: command the patient to shave their forehead, and then make an incision in the middle of the forehead, a small one in width (beginning from the fissure on the left temple towards the right temple; and the incision should go through the bone; extend your hand between the temples where chewing takes place), until the bone is exposed.
Dry all the blood with a sponge or a dry cloth, and then apply between the two edges of the incision a piece of old linen or cloth. And then apply powder mixed with vinegar and oil so that it does not lead to an infected abscess.
And when you release this and see that the abscess has already diminished, then cover it by scraping the bone until new flesh begins to form, and afterwards treat it with a drying regimen such as making plaster from two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colocynth mixed together, which should be applied to these wounds where new flesh is growing.
Chapter VI.
On the treatment of what affects the ears.
Any cause that affects the ears is one of four types: either it is a mineral stone or something resembling a stone such as iron or wood, or it is from a plant such as chaff or beans, or it is a fluid substance like water and vinegar or similar liquids, or some kind of animal.
And when a stone affects the ear or any other cause similar to those mentioned that does not adhere but rather lodges in the ear, then expose the ear to the sun, and if you see the stone, at that time drop into it some substance of violet oil or cumin, and subsequently administer its extraction with conditions, and make the patient sneeze by inducing a sneezing fit, and plug the nose upon the occurrence of sneezing. And then place around the opening of the ear some pieces of cloth or wool, and extend the ear to the upper parts, as it often helps with these causes.
And if it is not expelled, then administer its extraction with the instrument called a gentil epistilus, which has the following form:
And if it is expelled with the instrument, that is good; and if not, then administer its extraction with a thin piece of wood through slight manipulation.
And if it is not expelled by these methods, then make a tube of reed and insert one end of the tube into the ear canal, and seal around the tube with wax and softened oil so that nothing else enters except through the tube. From this excerpt taken from the text on veins with strong attraction, for troops accustomed as we have recounted.
If it is not forgotten in this manner, now take a thin piece of wood or a small apparatus with which birds are usually caught, a small amount, and place that at the end of the vein, and then wrap that area carefully placed. And then insert it into the opening of the ear with ease, and then dry the ear of its humidity.
And thus if it is not forgotten with all the causes that we have recounted, now you should proceed to incise that area which has become inflamed or spasmodic.
And the method of incising that area is to begin by puncturing the diseased vein and extracting the blood according to the method appropriate for it, and then make a small cut between your fingers and turn the ear towards you, and make a small fissure at the edge of the ear where it is most prominent. And let the incision be in a crescent shape until it reaches the stone, and when the stone is located, remove it if possible with appropriate instruments; and then close the incision quickly at that moment, and care for it until it is healed.
And if the cause in the ear is one of the growths that have become inflamed, now administer the treatment and the extraction of it; but if you do not proceed accordingly, then take fine cotton wadding in this form: and administer the removal of that growth which has become lodged in the ear.
If you do not want to use water when you think that it is already moistened by the vapor from the ear, place it in small pieces, and extract them with hooks or with subtle instruments, as we have said, for the extraction must be gentle.
In the water that has entered into the ear, it is beneficial for the patient to use sneezing with a mixture at the beginning, and fill their other ear with some old cloth, and then lay on the side where the water is. If this dislodges the water, it is good; otherwise, take smooth stones or lemons according to the length of a finger, heat them in the fire for a little while, and have the patient insert one of those into their ear canal and jump with the affected side down, striking another stone against the heated stone that is inside the ear. Do not remove the stone until all the water is expelled.
Do not remove the stone until all the water is expelled. And the water will be expelled in this way: take paper or cotton, place one end of it in the ear and hold the other end over a flame until it burns away.
And place another piece of cotton in and do this as many times as necessary until all the water is expelled, and squeeze it with a cannula as was mentioned above regarding the extracting stone.
In the extraction of an animal entering the ear, if it is a small object, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is a large object that causes pain to the patient, then administer the extraction with instruments and hooks, and the cause of this is more serious than all other causes that enter the ear.
In the extraction of a worm generated in the ear, when you treat it as we have said in the division and in the tractate on distillations and do not confound your treatment, then you should expose the ear to the sun.
And if any cause of the worms appears here, then extract that am or thin am, but if no cause appears, then take a tube narrow below and wide above, which has this shape: And insert the slender end into the ear according to the amount that suffices for the patient; and then suck out the am with great suction, and do this several times until all the worms are expelled.

Take what is enclosed in the ear and heat it a little over fire. And be careful that the substance you will apply in the ear is not too irritating, for medicines for the ear cannot tolerate this.
Chapter VII.
On the treatment of blocked ears.
Sometimes infants are born with their ears not perforated, and this also happens in some adults, where the ear canal is blocked by an infection or flesh growing there; and this blockage sometimes occurs at the entrance of the ear canal where it cannot be seen, and sometimes it is further inside.
And when it occurs at the entrance of the ear, where it cannot be seen, it is in the most difficult positions for easy treatment.
And when you can see it, have the patient expose the affected ear to the sun and observe it. And if you see an obstruction that is visible, open it with a fine probe of the following shape:
If the end of it is small in width, with one side sharp and the other not; and the probe should be two-sided so as not to injure the ear.
And if the blockage is due to flesh growing in the ear or in the ear canal, then use fine forceps and carefully cut away all the flesh.
And if the blockage is at the entrance of the ear, then take a thin needle and heat it slightly over fire, and then place it in the ear canal.
And thus if you have noticed that the swelling is on the side where the patient has more ease, due to the heaviness of hearing, it presses the swelling on that easier side; and be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear.
And then place in the ear a piece of cloth according to the quantity of the swelling which you have wrapped in Egyptian cotton; and do this for several days until you are sure of the consolidation of the swelling; or take something and push it into warm water and sprinkle it with finely ground powder and use it. And if you see that the ear is already abscessed, then you must remove what was there and replace it with another piece wrapped in wax mixed with rose oil, until the abscess has subsided; and afterward care for it until it is healed.
But if there is bleeding, then soak a sponge or cloth in cold water and place it on the ear, and use another treatment that stops the flow of blood, which is described in the chapter on distillation.
Chapter VIII.
On the treatment of boils that occur on the eyelids.
Boils that occur on the eyelids sometimes appear moist, and at other times they are dry.
Therefore, you should have these available either in tin or in ounce containers, and then sprinkle them finely over the affected areas, and afterward place something finely powdered on those spots.
But if pain and bleeding occur, then you should cauterize those areas with a fine cautery.
The best cautery is applied to incisions and grooves that return when the cause of them remains; and when these are burned with fire, those grooves are consumed and do not return.
Chapter IX.
Treatment for a condition that affects the eyelids.
Grooves appear in the eyelids due to some cause that resembles a serious condition in its strength and hardness, and therefore it is called a serious condition.
And it is an accumulation of thick moisture in the eyelid, both above and below.
Therefore, the treatment for this is to observe whether the condition has spread on the surface of the eyelid and has affected it entirely; and the cause of this is superficial.
Therefore, make an incision along the length of it, and then carefully remove it entirely with ease until it is completely extracted, and then stop the bleeding and close it.
And if the figure is large, then you adjust it with stitches; and take care of it until it is healed.
And if it is small, you will not have trouble with it because the warmth of it restores and heals it.
And if the condition is spreading to the inner parts of the eyelid, you should examine the inner surface, then lift the eyelid and stop the bleeding without making an incision, and press it entirely, and if the eyelid is stretched due to the incision, this is not noted as any cause.
At the beginning, wash the wound with salt water; and treat the area with water that promotes healing until it is healed.
Chapter 10.
About the treatment of a tumor above the eye socket.
A tumor is gray and originates in the layers of the upper eyelid, and it often affects children, worsening their wounds and leading to a severe attack of catarrh when they die; and they cannot look at the brightness of the sun because tears continuously flow from their eyes.
And for this reason they often lie with their faces covered, and they sleep with their faces covered; and the eyelashes of their lower lids are moist, which have been covered by inflammation, and the appearance of a tumor is apparent in the eye; and when you press the area with your fingers, you can feel a tumor inside.
And there is a method of operation for when the patient places their head in your lap, and you place a cloth over them and make a circle according to the amount it contains of all parts, and then place that on them and press with your fingers all around so that the tumor aggregates in the middle of the circle, and then introduce moisture into it using a spatula through a fissure along its length, but the fissure should not be larger than the one made in phlebotomy.
But in the initial incision, you should cut through the tissue completely until you reach the tumor, because in major procedures, you treat the tumor through a fissure according to the form of a white mass.
Therefore, extract that which is wrapped in the cloths among those you have wrapped around it from the sides and roll between your right and left hand until it is dispersed.
And be careful not to insert it into the crack so that the powder does not reach the wound and damage it.
But if it does not appear to you ready at the beginning of the crack, then insert into the crack a small piece that can be easily removed; and then extract it as we have said; and then immerse cloths in warm water and vinegar, place them over the area, and secure them with powder.
And some people sprinkle salt and place it in the deepest part of the crack so that what remains is free from moisture.
And then take care of it until it is healed.
But if an abscess occurs in the area, then treat it with soft plasters until it is healed.

Chapter XII.
On Removing Stinging Hairs from the Eye Using a Needle When the Hair is Embedded.
When there are unnatural, hard, rough, and stinging hairs in the eye, the operation is that you take a fine needle and place it on each hair gently and carefully, and then adjust the ends of them delicately. And let the length of the fields be one palm in quantity.
And below that, prepare another fine field briefly, and use the extremities of it if you wish.
And then place the malady at its head in your hand, and let it be close to the sun so that your work may be visible, for it is a subtle and delicate operation.
And then insert the needle into the base of the hair that requires removal and let it penetrate quickly into the eyelid before you extract it from above the natural hair.
And then pull the hair in from above and insert it into its place, and let there be one or two or three hairs and no more.
And then pull your hand in so that the hair is removed and placed back into its proper place on the eyelid with the natural hair.
But if it is placed back and the hair is not removed, pull it back to the sides below the field that you have prepared with it, so that it may be properly placed among the surrounding area.
And observe this with the eye's vision, for now you have placed back both the hair and the field, and stitch each part together, leaving the stitches for two or three days until the hair adheres to its place and grows on that good flesh.
And if the hair is too short, now attach a long hair from the natural hairs to it, or leave it for some time until it grows longer in its place, and then raise it.
Chapter XIII.
On the treatment of a swelling that occurs in the upper eyelid.
When there appears a swelling in the eye, which is a contraction of the eyelid when it is closed, either to the right or left side, due to poor healing of an injury, cutting, or cautery, and this is called leporine. This swelling can be either natural or accidental, caused by improper healing of wounds, cuts, or cauterizations, or similar injuries poorly treated.
The method of the operation is that you should cut open that contraction and separate its edges, then place between them a piece of linen cloth, and bind it there until it heals.
And it is not advisable to use treatments for it that dry or constrict, as if you do this, the swelling will return worse than before and never heal properly.
Use treatments that soften, such as fenugreek, and boil the leaves and seeds in water or use east wind, which should be mixed with some oil to liquefy it. Then soak a piece of cloth in this mixture and apply it for treatment.
The essence of your treatment is to ensure that you do not allow any part to become overly constricted and heal in a way that it does not maintain its original form.
And this operation that we have described is merely a correction of the swelling that does not return to its original form as it was before.
Chapter XIV.
On the treatment of ehacrati, which is done below the eyelid.
This ehacrati which is made below the eyelid, which is properly called ehacrati; and it is of some natural, others accidental.

And this figure is the Greek letter: lambda.
And then remove the flesh in the amount that is the width below it, which stiffens the eyelid.
And then adjust the separated parts and sew them together with linen thread; and then treat those as we have said about softening medicines and plasters until it is healed.
And if through incisions, either by a cut or suture or cauterization, you must now make an incision in a straight line along the edge of the eyelid as was previously described. And then separate the membrane between the two lips as we have said.
In the summary of the speech on the treatment of incisions when they are above or below, let it run in the operation according to how the preparation of the incision was made, and that is in a form of various patterns.

On the adherence of the eyelid to the conjunctiva or to the cornea.

Chapter XVI.

Chapter XVII.
On the incision of styes and what is born from flesh tightly attached to the eye.

Chapter XXIV.
On the treatment of wounds to the nose.
When in the nose there are various growths that differ from one another, among which is a cause that resembles the sting of a venomous insect or a polyp; and this disease is called polypus because it resembles the aforementioned condition.
