Chapter XXV.
Of thorns naturally found in the extremities of the nose.
Often there is a thorn naturally found in the extremities of the nose, and it is treated and removed on certain days within the period when such care is observed.
And for this reason you should incise that at the beginning of its appearance, and you should treat all of it. And then pause over the place where you cauterize or apply burning medicine, which is at that location.
But if the incision is delayed until it has become hardened, hard, dark in color, and with little sensation, then do not touch that with iron as it is a chronic abscess; for often such harm comes to those who incise this abscess improperly.
And if the abscess is due to touch and is not of a dark color, and sometimes incision is possible in all that area, then evacuate the pus and make an incision there without fear, and treat the place with something that dries it up until it is healed.
Chapter XXVI.
On suturing the nose and lips and the ear when the continuity is dissolved by plague or similar condition.
Know that when dissolution of continuity occurs in one of these cartilages, few will undertake such an operation except in some men.
Therefore, when there is any cause for these conditions, consider whether it is a fresh plague with its own blood, and then you should approximate the two lips of the wound with sutures, and afterward treat it until it is healed.
And if the lips of the continuity dissolution are already separated, and each is made healthy, then you should scrape each part of its visible edge until blood comes out. And then approximate the two lips with sutures and strengthen them, and over those apply powder of dragon's blood and sprinkle it, and place on top a piece of mastic plaster or some other consolidating plaster, and leave that dressing for two days or three, and then remove that and change the plaster and leave it until the pus is completely evacuated, and afterward treat with an ointment until it is healed.
But the method of suturing is that you approximate the dissolution of continuity either with needles as we have recommended for abdominal sutures, or approximate the dissolution to the pus as seems appropriate to you.
Chapter XXVII.
On the extraction of those causes that cause swelling in the two lips in the partitions within.
Often in some men there appear in the partitions within their lips certain hard swellings resembling the gristle of birds, and some of them are small and some are larger.
Therefore, you should turn the lips and cut into each of those hardnesses from all sides, and immediately fill the place with finely shredded cloth so that the blood is constricted, and then wash it well with something astringent, until it heals.
Chapter XXVIII.
On the incision of flesh that is adhered to the gums.
Often there arises on the gum flesh that is adhered to it, which the ancients called "albulus," then you should suspend that with incisions or with forceps and incise it down to its base, and allow the pus or blood to flow.
And then apply to the place finely shredded cloth or other astringent or drying powders.
And if that flesh returns, then incise it again, and cauterize it, for afterward the cauterization will prevent its return.
Chapter XXIX.
On the extraction of teeth with forceps.
When on the surface of the teeth in the partitions within and those outside, and between the adhered gums, there are rough spots, tartar deposits, and often they are blackened and become green or yellow due to corruption, causing the teeth to form tartar.
And so you should make the patient lie between your thighs and place his head in your lap, and cut the teeth from which these abscesses arise and cause sand-like substances to come out until none of them remain, and do this for blackness and yellowness and other such things until they are cleansed.
Then if it is still in the condition from the beginning of the treatment, that is good; but if not, at this time you repeat the treatment on those [teeth] on another day and on the second and on the third until it reaches the final stage as you wish.
And you should know that the teeth have the need for various forms of instruments and different shapes according to how they are prepared for your operation. And because the razor with which the tooth is cut from inside is different from the razor used to scrape between the teeth according to other forms, and these forms of razors you should prepare as you will see shortly:
Chapter XXX.
On the Extraction of Teeth.
When you treat the tooth of its pain with total gentleness and delay in its complete extraction, because there is no cause that can replace it once it is extracted, for it is a substance sublime that cannot be dispensed with in the extraction of it.
But when the patient is forced to have that tooth extracted, you must be firmly certain which tooth is painful, for many times the pain deceives the patient and he thinks it is in a healthy tooth, and you extract that one but immediately the pain does not cease until the diseased and painful tooth is extracted, as we have already seen by the operation of barbers.
Thus when you are satisfied which is the painful tooth, and once you know well, it is necessary that you incise around the tooth with a spatula of some virtue, until it dissolves from the tooth the gum entirely, and then remove it with your said tools or with fine forceps little by little until you have removed it completely.
And then use strong pincers for good leverage or a firm grip, and place the head of the patient between your knees so that you have it well without hurting them, and then pull the tooth straight in such a way that you do not break it, nor cause greater pain to the patient.
And so if it is not loose, now take one of those instruments and place it underneath from all sides with ease and exert effort to remove the tooth as was done at the beginning.
But if the tooth is fractured or decayed, now you must cover that fracture with cloth and secure it at the end with a thin thread so that it does not break during your compression on it with forceps.
And you must act carefully when incising around the entire circumference of the gum and guard against using too much force so that you do not break it or leave part of it behind, and return to the patient because of the malice that it be better than the initial pain of it.
And be careful not to do what some ignorant barbers do in their attempt and audacity during the extraction, without administering what we have recommended; for many times they cause great evils to sick people which are harder to treat, and the roots of them exposed entirely, or some of them, or that you extract it with some bones of the jaw as many times we have witnessed.
And after the extraction let the mouth be washed either with vinegar or with something agreeable mixed with salt.
And if blood flows because of this, just as you do for similar wounds, then apply some quantity of wax and sprinkle it over the wound, and if that does not suffice, cauterize.
The shape of the forceps and holding them delicately with which the tooth is grasped at the beginning should be long in length, short in handle, and thick, so that they do not bend when using them to work.
And they should be like rings with thick handles such that when you grasp them, they are not bent; their extremities should be short.
And they should be made of Indian iron with straight extremities, and at the extremities of those there should be teeth, some of which fit into others and grasp firmly by constriction, and sometimes the extremities of those are in the shape of a bird's beak called ciconia, which is a hawk, and they are very strong in their grip.
Chapter XXXI.

When you need to extract a tooth that is attached for some reason, it is advisable to place a poultice on the area for one day or two until the site becomes softened; and afterward use such forceps or holders with extremities shaped like the beak of a bird called ciconia or hawk, the shape of the forceps:
Their extremities should be treated internally as well as externally.

And let it be of short thick length, and do not hide it so that it does not rattle.

But the skilled and subtle artisan discovers for himself according to what he understands from the operation and various diseases; for there are diseases about which the ancients did not say or leave a proper instrument, due to their diverse forms.

If there is only a small abscess in the bone, then remove that part which is abscessed and discolored, and treat it until it is healed.
Chapter XXXII.
On the treatment of teeth that protrude beyond the others.
When teeth protrude beyond their natural alignment and especially when this happens to women, particularly to those of advanced age; therefore, you should consider: if a tooth is too close to another tooth and it is impossible to file or cover it, then remove that tooth; but if it is not attached to the adjacent tooth, then cut it with an instrument of this shape; it resembles a pig’s snout and is made of Indian iron with a very sharp point.
And when your incision is made such that you cut it over several days due to the hardness of the tooth, and ensure that it does not become inflamed or affect other teeth.
And if the protruding tooth can be filed down, then file it with an iron rasp of this shape:
And let it be of Indian iron and the margua exactly; and let it be of small points as well, like a file with which needles are made, on which the tooth is filed little by little over several days with ease, so that it may not become another tooth or be deformed. And apply strips to it at the end, and shave it with razors.
And if it is a tooth of which a part is broken and the tongue touches it, now you must file away that inside where the sharpness of that fracture is, until it is smoothed and evened out, so that the tongue does not hurt itself and the speech is not impaired.
Chapter XXXIII.
On the restoration of deformed teeth with gold or silver filling.
When it happens that the front teeth are loosened and moved by impact or accident, and the patient cannot bite on what they eat, and you have treated them with astringent medicines, but your treatment has not been effective, now in order to prevent them from falling out, you should reinforce those that are stable with gold filling and not silver, because silver can turn green and after some days it may fall off, whereas gold never changes.
And let the filling be in such subtlety and thickness according to the quantity that can enter between the teeth; and the form of the restoration is that you take the filling and place twice as much between two healthy teeth, and then build up with two tortuositates of the filling between one or multiple deformed teeth, until it reaches the adjacent healthy tooth on the other side. From there proceed with the tissue into the part from which you began, and stretch your hand with ease and skill so that it is not harmed.
And let your thread be such that when you stretch the fiber of the teeth, it does not escape.
And then cut off the excess part of the thread using forceps or scissors, and attach it at each place with your fingers, and twist and hide it between the healthy tooth and the damaged tooth, so that it does not cause injury to the tongue. And then sew it as tightly as a Roman would.
But if it comes loose or breaks, stretch that or those again with another thread throughout its time.
And this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the alignment of two healthy teeth and two damaged teeth, as you see them tied:
And when it happens that you return one tooth or two near their proper places, and they grow back as we have recommended, and they heal.
And only skilled artisans and wise practitioners can do this.
And sometimes a similar shape is made from the bone of an animal, and it is placed in the location where the tooth is missing, and it is stretched as we have said, and remains and serves there for a long time.
Chapter XXXIV.
On the incision of the band that goes around the tongue and prevents speech.
This ligature which was mentioned above the tongue either belongs to those that one is born with and are natural or are accidental and occur due to a disease that has already healed.
And the operation is such that men open the mouth of the patient, and place their hand inside; then they raise the tongue, and then cut that nerve ligament horizontally within so that the tongue may be freed from its attachment.
But if there is any hardness or node in that area, and this has remained due to the healing of an injury, then you should incise it and cut along the horizontal so that you have separated the ligament and dissolved the node.
And be careful not to make a cut in the surface of the skin so that you do not sever here an artery and cause bleeding.
And then wash the remnants of the incision with cold water or vinegar or salt water; and afterwards place a piece of linen under the tongue; thus, the patient should hold the tongue down against something each night so that it does not heal in another manner.
But if bleeding occurs, apply over the area vitriol powder; but if the blood flows continuously, then cauterize the area with a hot iron, which is appropriate for this. And then proceed with the treatment using other methods until it is healed.
Chapter XXXV.
On the Extraction of a Ranula Below the Tongue.
At times, an abscess appears below the tongue, resembling a small swelling that impedes the tongue from its natural movement; and it grows so much within a short time that it fills the mouth.
In the operation where you have the mouth of the patient sixty degrees toward the sun and observe the abscess.
And if you see it of dark color or black, hard, in which the patient does not feel sensation, then do not touch that which is gangrenous.
And if it is inclined towards whiteness, in which there is moisture, then you place the incision in that area, and cut with a fine scalpel, and cut it from all sides; and if blood flows during the time of your operation, then pause and apply three times vinegar, which is vitriol, until the blood is restrained.
And then return to your work until you have properly treated it, and wash it with vinegar and salt; and care for it with the other treatment until it is healed.
Chapter XXXVI.
On the extraction of abscesses from both ears and those that are in the throat and other abscesses.
When you encounter an abscess in the throat, which are glands that are somewhat assembled together, some of which appear outside and are called the tonsils. When you treat them as we have said in the division and they do not heal, then consider if the abscess is hard, dark colored, with little sensation; then do not touch that part with iron.
And if it is of red color and the base is thick, then do not touch that part with iron due to the flow of blood; rather, let it remain until it has matured, and then either you will remove it or it will burst on its own.
And if it is of white color, hard, and the edge of it is subtle, then that is what should be cut into.
And the operation on it is to consider before your operation whether the abscess of it has healed after cauterization or if it has been reduced in some way; and then make the patient sit facing the sun, and his head should be turned towards you, and hold open the mouth of it, and the assistant takes with his fingers the tongue down with an instrument of noble material which has this form:
And it should be made of silver or iron, and it should be thin like a knife.
Then as you press with that the tongue and the abscess is shown to you, look directly at it with your own vision, then take some of it and place it in an almond, and pull it out to the sides as much as you can. Or take some other cause of the tunics, and then cut it with an instrument which has this form:
Or take some other cause of the tunics, and then cut it with an instrument which has this form: and it resembles forceps, however the ends of it are curved, thus that the opening of each of those is in line with the other, sharp, made of iron.
But if this instrument is not present for you, then cut it with a scalpel which has this form: It should be sharp on one side and not sharp on the other side.
And after you have cut one side, cut the other in the same manner of cutting, and then the patient should rinse with water.
If blood flows, guard and use water of the decoction of haws or myrtle leaves and similar to those styptic causes until the flow of blood is restrained, and afterward cure it until it is healed.
And sometimes pus appears in the groin or other abscesses or those two armpits, and incise them as is said about the incision of two breasts similarly.
And I had treated a woman with an abscess which had appeared in her groin, the abscess was tending to a dark color and was insensitive, it had already closed her groin, and the woman was breathing very narrowly, and I had prohibited her from eating and drinking water, and she would have been near death if I had not intervened for one day or two.
And the abscess had swollen so much that it formed two ridges from which pus flowed out through two openings.
Then I decided to operate immediately and inserted my finger into one of the openings, and extracted that, and then I incised at the base of the other opening, and then I closed it, and compressed its tongue, and then I placed the plug in that abscess.
And then I excised a large part of it, and only a little blood flowed from it. Then the groin of that woman was absolutely fine, and she began to drink water immediately, and soon after ate food. Therefore, I did not need to incise that abscess again for a long time, and subsequently an abscess appeared in its place, which I had to incise to prolong its healing.
Thus I cut and cauterized the wound of his leg, thus ending the procedure; and afterwards I walked around not knowing what God had done for him at that time.
Chapter xxxvii.
On the incision of an apostemated swelling.
When one calls to the swelling, and it is apostemated and elongated, it is then called perpendicular; and if it is below thick and round, it is then called a bubba.
But when it is cured with what we have said in the division, and your treatment does not conform to it, and also when the apostema cauterized remains subtle, then you should incise the one that is aggregated and round; and if it extends in length, and is sanguineous, of dark or black color, and is not central, then you should attempt its incision because there is fear of malady in such cases.
And when you see it according to the method I have described regarding its whiteness and length, make the patient sit down and press your tongue against it with an instrument that reveals its form and then place the thumb on one side, pull it downward, and incise it with one of two instruments mentioned in the double incision procedure.
And you should not incise it beyond what is appropriate according to the natural term without cause, for if you incise too much, you will harm the patient.
And after the incision, use what we have recommended for the double incision procedure, and care for it until it is healed.
If the patient is afraid of the incision, use an instrument in the cauterization of him without fear, and the way of the cautery on him is nothing but sharp water, and that you place the head of the patient on your thigh, and then press his tongue with the instrument which we have mentioned, and then take the water which we have said in the chapter on cauterization, and confirm it with this cause living, and place it neither thick nor thin, and with that fill the concavity of the instrument which has this form:
Let the extremity of the instrument be such that it is placed in the cavity as with a ladle's concavity, and place the instrument with the medicine on the tongue, and the patient lies on his back so that saliva or mucus from the mouth can flow due to the intrinsic medicine, so that none of this flows out from any cause onto him and thus causes harm.
And then touch it with your hand on the medicine, and press that onto the uvula for half an hour until you see it become blackened and numbed by the bite of the medicine.
And if you want, take a cloth and wrap it around the end of the reed, and dip the cloth in the medicine, and insert the reed with the cloth into a tube so that the cloth adheres to that tube, and do this many times until you achieve what you desire from the cauterization of the uvula, and then leave it as it dries and falls off after three or four days.
And if you need to repeat the medicine, do so, and after the cauterization wipe around the uvula with a cloth dipped in honey, and modify it with that which is around it from the medicine, and wash it with wiping water, and treat it outside with embrocation, and take care of it with bandages until it heals.
And this kind of treatment is safer than incision and less painful from fear.
In some cases, the uvula is treated with something that is milder than cauterization and incision. It is cured by sublimation in this manner: take a poultice of ysope, origany, rue, Arabian saffron, chamomile, ground seeds similar to these herbs, and adjust all these causes or some of them into a flask, which should be submerged in sweet wine and boiled. The flask should be heated moderately, and in the middle of the flask place a tube made like this; it is made of silver or reed.
And insert the end into the mouth of the patient so that the vapor reaches the uvula, until the uvula is sufficiently treated.
And repeat this procedure several times until it is dry. Be careful not to perform this treatment at the beginning of the onset of abscesses, as it would be too harsh for the abscess. You should not do this; instead, you must declare the abscess before cauterizing.
But if this instrument is not available to you, take a cane and attach a hollow tube at the end of it, so that the mouth of the patient is covered, as the hollow of the tube prevents the vapor from entering the mouth.
And this treatment is good for health.
Chapter XXXVIII.
On the extraction of thorns and what adheres to the gums and other causes.
Move carefully around the collarbone or spine of the patient or for some other reason.
Then look at what is visible among those things, upon which your eyes focus, and then press the tongue with an instrument in front of sunlight so that it may be revealed to you what is in the throat.
And that which does not appear and is hidden in the throat, try to make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach, because a strong cause adhering near the throat will easily be expelled by vomiting; or have the patient swallow a piece of bread or some lettuce leaves or a dry biscuit; or give the patient a piece of dried sea sponge, and bind it tightly with honey, then let the patient swallow that, as it passes to the place where sharp spines are and is extracted, thus it will be easily expelled. And take an eel and bind it with honeyed thread, then place it inside and gradually extract it; or take a probe and gently insert and gradually move it.
And if it is not expelled using the methods we have mentioned, then use an instrument made of lead in this form:
And let it be as thick as a small reed, and at the end of it there should be a curved part that you can easily insert into their throat with ease.
And let the patient lie with their head raised up, and be careful not to touch the bone of the throat, so that it does not injure the patient or cause pain to the bone or spine, or allow the physician's hand to do so.
However, let the surgeon use honey, because of his knowledge of the place where the cause is attached and embedded inwards, and he inserts his hand with the instrument into it, all this according to the quantity which has been prepared for him until it is expelled.
Chapter xxxix.
On the Extraction of a Bloodsucker Attached to the Throat.
When treating a bloodsucker with what we have mentioned in the division of treatment with medicines and not compresses, consider the time of day when the patient's throat is exposed to the sun, after you have loosened their tongue with the instrument that we recommended.
Then when you see the bloodsucker, remove it gently with a small incision or with subtle gestures carefully.
And if it is not possible for you to remove it then, take a concave tube and insert it into the patient's throat, and immediately place a heated iron in the concavity of the tube, and do this as many times (until the bloodsucker is dead and falls out of the throat) and keep the patient from water for the entire day.
And then take a vessel full of warm water and open the patient's mouth over it, and wash the mouth with it; and do not let anything from it pass through, but pour out the water one hour after another with your hand, as soon as the bloodsucker feels the water, it will grasp onto it.
However, if it is not expelled with what we have recommended, then smoke the patient with cymin or with asafetida using the instrument that we recommended for smoking the uvula.
In this, so in what case.
And there is another method of operation in suffigation with that one, which is that you take a jar in which are burning coals and the jar is covered by a cloth in the middle of which is a hole, and it is prepared on that hole the end of the instrument; and then place the suffigation above it; and have the patient put his mouth at the end of the tube, and close his mouth so that the suffigation does not escape until you know that the suffigation has reached the blood-sucker, for the blood-sucker will immediately fall.
And if it does not work, now you repeat the suffigation several times, and abstain the patient from drinking, and give dry foods like salted almonds, and do not let him drink water, and in this regimen it is necessary that he be kept.
And this is the form of the instrument with which the blood-sucker is treated when it is seen in the throat; and it resembles forceps as you might see them, but it has some curvature. which is placed in the throat, and the end of it resembles the beak of a heron, which is sharpened with a file, so that when it presses against something, it does not slip.
Chapter 40.
In which is the summary of the discourse on the preparation for abscesses and their incision.
Abscesses are of various kinds, in many ways, as will be recalled for each one in this book.
And there are various ways of puncturing and incising them by two methods, one of which is for the specific type of abscess within itself; and by what they draw from the humidity.
And the second method is for the locations where accidents occur in the body, for an abscess that occurs in the head is different from one that occurs in the buttocks; and an abscess that occurs in a fleshy location is different from one that occurs at a joint; and each has its own treatment through surgery.
And there are some abscesses that should not be punctured but left until the pus has properly matured or they have reached a suitable condition.
And there are other abscesses that should be evacuated when they are crosswise and not mature according to their proper condition, such as those near joints, because when an abscess approaches a joint, its nature is prolonged into the surrounding area, and if it corrupts the ligaments or nerves of that joint, it becomes a cause for contraction of that limb; or it may be close to a principal member, and if you delay puncturing it until it matures, it will harm the principal member; or it may be near the buttocks, so puncture it before it matures; but do not puncture it when it is raw, due to incomplete digestion, except for that which is near the buttocks, so that you do not cause a prepuce and extend it into the inner parts of the buttocks, thereby creating a fistula, or leave it until it heals improperly. It is important that you know the right time to puncture the abscess, and this is when it has matured.
And you should know that it is mature when there is relief from pain and the cessation of fever, along with a decrease in hardness and pulse, and the sharpness at the head of the abscess, as well as other signs.
And you should know that the incision must be made in the place where the pus is below the abscess and coming from the swelling.
And the incision should always be made along the length of the flesh or body if the abscesses are in the parts of the arms or legs, and in places like joints, tendons, nerves, arteries; and finally, in all similar locations where there is no reflection; for in those that reflect, use an incision according to that member.
But when the abscess is in a fleshy area, it is better to delay the incision until the digestion of the second stage is confirmed, as we have said; for if you make an incision before that, the course of the patient's illness will be prolonged and more severe filthiness will result, and thus the lips of the abscess will become hardened and its depth increased.
But some abscesses should be incised according to the width of the flesh or body due to necessity, or according to what that member requires.
And you should administer a small incision in small abscesses, and in large abscesses a larger or wider incision, or multiple sections according to the diversity of the size of the abscesses.
And in other abscesses where it is necessary for the condition to be excavated and incised, when it is done as if with bread and is completed at a time when it already exists, just as in the case of those that occur too frequently like boils and buboes.
And of those that are incised in a section having three corners; and of those where it is incised as if in the shape of a maple leaf, such as the abscesses of the armpits.
And there are those in which a round section and a crescent-shaped section are administered, and similar ones to those.
But in the case of one that is not a core as are superficial abscesses and tumors, you should puncture it with a superficial incision or simply scrape it.
And when the abscess is large and has collected pus, you should puncture it but do not hesitate to extract all the pus at that time; having extracted a portion from it, on another day scrape the abscess inside, and then extract a larger portion, and continue doing this several times according to its degree until it is healed.
And especially if the patient is a robust man, or a pregnant woman, or an infant, or an old person in debility, for the vital spirit in such cases is easily resolved by the evacuation of the pus, and the patient may die quickly, so you operate on them carefully.
Therefore, guard this chapter with great caution, and when you make the puncture in which you puncture these abscesses, you should clean the plaques and then consider whether the plaque of the abscess is small or a flat section; if so, you administer some of it or antiseptic cotton. If the abscess is large and the cracks from the puncture are many, then you should apply medicated plasters to each one until they heal.
And if in the abscess a part of the cord is divided or has been hollowed out around its circumference, then you should pack it with old cotton or thread made from linen, as when you have treated pustules or boils without moisture; and strengthen that on the third day; and then proceed to treat it according to what is needed from ointments until it is healed.
If blood flows during the time of your operation, then administer water, wash and prepare cloths in which you dip a cloth, and place that over the location of the bleeding for several times.
If the bleeding persists, then you should administer treatment and cure with powders which I have recommended in various places of this our book and division.
If it is in the time of winter, and the location of the abscess is near many nerves, then you should infuse powders in vinegar and cauterized oil, and place those on the locations.
And if it is in summer, and the locations are fleshy, then you should place powders mixed with water and oil or with vinegar and oil, and let all of this be washed internally for three days as we have said. Then you should open the abscess, cleanse it, and administer to its cure what suits it until it is healed.
And this is what is necessary for the knowledge of the cure of abscesses universally, but according to the method of distinction I have already said about every abscess in which manner the way of its cure is by separate chapters.
Chapter 41.
On the section of abscesses that appear on the neck.
In the neck of the head, small abscesses appear, and there are various types of nodes that contain tunics; and the types of these nodes are many.
And they are soft, and contain moisture similar to jelly. Of those things which contain moisture like dust, and similar to them; and of those things which are stony and hard.
And in the section of all things, and in the extraction of those, there is no fear, as the extraction of those does not contradict nature.
And the operation in the section of those is that you express them with an instrument whose form approaches this, which is called an entromes, until you know what it contains.
For if what it contains is moisture, then you should divide that with a section according to its length by making a superficial section according to this form:
And begin the section from the line of .B. to the line of .G. When the moisture has been evacuated, then you should excise that skin which contains the moisture, and do not leave any part of it behind, for if any part remains, it may cause issues later on.
And then immerse the piece in Egyptian oil if it is available, and if not, in salt water. Fill the wound with this and leave it for another day, for this will dissolve all that remains of the membrane.
And then apply the Egyptian oil to that piece again, thoroughly and repeatedly if necessary, until you are confident that there is no remaining part of the membrane. Then care for the wound with the oil until it is healed.
And if an abscess contains hard nodes, then you should incise it according to this form: with a section having the shape of a cross, and insert once between the two lips of the incision and scrape it thoroughly, and exert your effort in extracting the membrane that contains it.
If it happens that you encounter opposition in surgery, now do what I have recounted first of all.
And similarly, treat the suppurated abscess by incision and cure as we have told you; and the incision of a suppurated abscess is easier because it contains little blood and less moisture.

Chapter XLIX.
On the Incision of Abscesses That Occur Due to Artery or Vein.
When an artery is ruptured and the surrounding area has become inflamed, an abscess may occur. The signs by which it can be known whether inflammation and abscess are due to an artery or a vein: for when the abscess is due to an artery, it tends to aggregate in the front part of the body; and if you press on the abscess with your fingers, you will hear a hissing sound.
And an abscess due to a vein is round and appears on the surface of the body.
And the incision for this abscess is dangerous, especially in areas behind the armpits, in the angles, and in the neck, as it can be quite risky; therefore, its treatment should generally be avoided. For those that occur in the extremities or on the head, it should also be avoided.
May it be done upon him who is of this due to inflation of the artery opening; cut in the dry section along its length; and near the incision with an inch or so from the artery, and release the tunics until it is uncovered.

And then press the place which is between two ligaments with a spatula so that the blood escapes entirely from it, and let the abscess be dissolved.
And then administer treatment in which pus is generated so that the ligaments fall off; and afterwards treat that with appropriate poultices until it is healed.
And if it is an abscess due to a vein section, then you should have in your hand what is possible of the abscess at that site, and afterwards insert the needle below the place where you had held with your hand, and make it penetrate; and tie it off double with thread so that you can extract it from the other side, and then ligate the abscess with a strong bandage as I have told you regarding the grapevine bandage on both sides of the thread's ends.
And if you fear that the thread might be extracted, then insert a knot with the needle below the entire abscess beyond the initial insertion of the needle, and tie four knots.
And then dry the abscess in its middle part so that when what is inside has come out, you then incise the excess tissue, and leave what is attached.
Then pause and apply powder which you have mixed with vinegar and oil, then proceed to give the treatment which is done with cauterization and bandages until it is healed.
Chapter on the abscess which occurs due to twisting of the nerves.

Chapter LII.
On the treatment of a hernia of the navel.
A hernia of the navel is caused by various reasons; either through fissures in the abdomen above the belly, and from it comes the membrane or bladder as in other ruptures; or due to a wound from which blood flows from a vein or artery depending on what is present there; or due to trapped air.
But if it is due to a fissure in the abdomen and the protrusion of the membrane, then the color of the swelling is similar to the color of the body; it causes little pain, and subsequently appears in various situations. And if it is due to the protrusion of the bladder, then its condition differs greatly from what we have described, and when you press on it with your fingers, it retreats; and quickly returns afterwards. It is light in weight and becomes prominent especially after bathing and hard work.
May it be if by moisture, the hours are like a lion and are not hidden when pressed with your hand, nor are they restrained, nor are they created.
And if it is by infection, the hours with these signs appear as an abscess turning black.
May it be if it is by flesh that has decayed, the abscess is severe, large and hard, and is situated in proportion to a quantity.
May it be if it is due to gas, then the touch of it is like a lion.
And the operation on it is that you consider whether the prominence of the navel is due to an infection from an artery, or a vein, or gas; then you should be cautious about treating it, for there is fear and dread as I have taught you in the chapter where I have described abscesses from arteries and veins.
And if the prominence of the navel is due to the intestine or the membrane, then you should command the patient to lie on their back and stand extended; then press your finger around the circumference of the entire navel, and then command them to lie face up with their hands under their buttocks; then surround it with a piece of linen about an inch wide around the circumference of the navel where you have marked with your finger; and then extend half of the abscess upwards from this point by about one inch; and then tie it around the circumference with strong thread or cloth in a proper manner.
And then open the center of the abscess over the dressing and insert your finger into that area to check for the intestine; and if you find it adhered or protected by the dressing, then carefully remove it and push the intestine towards the inner parts of the abdomen.
And if you have found the cloth, then take one ounce of it; and incise the excess.
And if it is contrary to your artery or vein, then encircle that spot, and return to your operation; take two needles and place in those two strong threads and insert the two needles into the circuit which you have made around the abscess in a crisscross manner, which you should make penetrate; and then compress the abscess into four parts over the needles.
And if you wish, remove the needles and leave the area open so that the extended flesh can drain and fall off by itself; or incise it when it is thin enough to drain, and then treat it with a lotion from among those mentioned until it is healed.
And if the prominence of the navel is of flesh or due to moisture, then you should treat the abscess as we have said and extract the blood or moisture that you find there, and then treat it with a lotion that will heal and consolidate the area.

Chapter LXII.
Of the section on treating hernias.
A hernia is nothing but an aggregation of moisture in the white tissue below the arch of the groin muscles, which is called a sac.

And if the moisture is in the proper inguinal region, then the abscess appears round at the part of the groin, and for this reason one estimates that it is another groin.
And if the moisture is between the ligament of the genitalia and the white fat, then it lies below the center.

And then take the cautery and place it on the prominent part of the sphincter, and press it to the pain in the abdomen.
And then cut the two prominent parts above the tip of the sphincter, and join them with sutures one to the other.
And then extract the tip of the sphincter, and do not cut it completely from the sphincter, nor extend the tissue, nor any other cause such as I will explain to you in the treatment of intestinal hernia.
And then treat it as you would a wound, and when you incise the abscesses, clean it and restore the wound until it is healed; for the sphincter is contracted and the swelling of rupture is not adjusted.
And cautery is better in this case, for it is closer to healing.
Chapter LXVIII.
On the Softening of the Cord of the Testicles.
In many cases, the cord of the testicles is softened because the flesh within it is also softened, and this requires careful management.
Therefore, it is necessary for the one seeking its cure to lay the patient according to his position, and then raise the entire cord that is softened above the natural cord; and then adjust two edges with sutures.
And if you wish, in the beginning, remove the excess of the softened cord with three or four stitches and secure it firmly with sutures.
Then incise between the sutures; and subsequently treat for other injuries until he is healed and the pus has subsided.
Chapter LXIX.
On Castration.
Know that castration in our law is excommunicated, yet for certain reasons it has been read to me and I remember it in this book; and the remembrance of it is not necessary except in two ways: one being so that when asked about it, the physician knows how to cure those who suffer from it; and the other way is that we often have a need for castration in other animals for our benefit, such as horses, oxen, pigs, and similar beasts.
And therefore, I say that castration is performed in two ways: either by crushing or by cutting.
In the case of that which is done by incision, the way to proceed is that we should cut the animal in warm water until its genitals are softened and loosened and hang down. And then take those with your hand inside until they are relaxed and do not appear below the touch.
In the case of castration done by rupture and section, make sure you hold the animal and press the root of its testicles with your left hand.
And then grasp the suspensory ligaments, and incise each one with a section until two processes are carried out.
And then incise those parts that you have each peeled back. And do not leave on those of the spermatic cord any cause for harm, but rather the fine cord that is over the vessels.
And this method of castration is better than the one done by incision, because incision often leaves some cause from the testicles for which the animal desires to copulate.
And then take care of the wound until it is healed.
Chapter 70.
On the treatment of hermaphroditism.
Hermaphroditism in men occurs in two ways: one is when it appears in the space between the root of the testicles, in the area between two testicles where there is a figure resembling that of a female, including hair.
In some cases of that vein which carries urine from which is in the cord of the testicles.
In women there is a special case: the womb of a woman above the pubis is like two testicles of a man, a little more towards the inside just as the buttocks of a man and two testicles.
The treatment is of three kinds: two for men and one kind for women. It is that you should incise those tight tissues so that the pus escapes from it, and then treat it as you would other wounds.
And in the second kind for men, of which you have urine that is in the cord of the testicles, there is no treatment or operation for it.
Chapter XXI.
About hemorrhoids and protruding flesh due to causes in women.
Severe hemorrhoids are tightly attached due to natural causes, making it difficult to treat and requiring careful management; in some cases, they become enlarged in women to such an extent that they prolapse similarly to men's and cause issues during intercourse.
Then you should grasp the excess of hemorrhoid with your hand or with forceps and incise it.
And do not incise excessively, especially near the root, so that it does not cause bleeding.
And then treat it as you would other wounds until it is healed.
This flesh that emerges is the flesh born in the cavity of the major part within which it fills, and it easily spreads to the parts outside according to the appearance of a tail (and thus I first called this "tail illness"); therefore, we must cut it as we would with an intestine, and treat what lies inside until it be healed.
Chapter LXXII.
On the Treatment of Abscesses.
Abscess is what occurs when the female organ is not perforated or the passage is small. And it can be either natural or accidental.
It is accidental due to a previous illness, and that is caused either by flesh that is too tight or by a thin or thick obstruction.
It occurs either in the front part of the major organ, or on its sides, or in the upper part of it, or in the lower part, and it prohibits intercourse, conception, and childbirth, and also easily prevents menstruation.
And the diagnosis of that condition is made by examination with a speculum, if the obstruction is apparent, proceed immediately; but if it is not apparent, then inquire about it through your questions or with an instrument.
But if the obstruction is due to a thin membrane and it is located between the two lips, then you should examine and rupture that.
And you should place pillows on both lips, and then gently place your fingers between them to examine.
And the woman should lie on her back, with her legs spread apart, and then gently spread the two lips to rupture that thin membrane and open the obstruction.
Take then the bandage and immerse it in oil and place that over the area, and change it daily so that the incised area does not become consolidated.
If the swelling is large and thick, now you should incise it with a scalpel or with a myrtle leaf.
If the obstruction is due to food, now suspend it for an hour, and then incise it.
And use the medicines that stop blood flow from a bite, such as hystiatia, dragon's blood, and onions, mixed with egg white.
Then administer a lead tube that is wide so that the wound does not consolidate too quickly.
And keep that for several days and administer dry heat to it.
And then treat it with the other method of consolidation until it is healed.
And sometimes it happens in the larger birth of other tissues, and now you should incise according to this method. But if it is due to a chronic abscess, then with the chronic abscess that is in the larger area, do not make any opposition with iron in any way.
Chapter LXXIII.
On the treatment of hemorrhoids and similar conditions that occur in the anus of women.
Hemorrhoids are an appreciation of the openings of small veins from which blood flows continuously; and as for old hemorrhoids, they form tumors.
Here I have said in the division of the species of those and the signs of those, and to say also those that receive cure and those that do not receive cure.
Therefore, I say that hemorrhoids and piles which are only in the region of the greater and do not appear to the touch, at this time it is not possible to perform cure with iron.
But those which are in the opening of the anus, on which one can feel by touch, these are those that can be treated.
And it is necessary that you place the woman in a sitting position to wash and then extend the hemorrhoid with forceps, or with a rough cloth, and incise those with razors.
And then powder should be applied to those areas that stop the flow of blood from one of the powdered substances used for incisions without chewing, such as acacia and similar ones.
And then bind the area with a dressing for one hour, and afterward place it in cold water.
And if the flow of blood persists, then have the area treated with a decoction of sumac and rind of lemons and gallnuts and similar substances.
And then take flour of barley and apply it with honey and sour wine to make a plaster on the back of it.
And if the blood is congealed, that is good; and if not, apply it to two sides, and at the nipples without incision.
And then take wool and apply it to the area with juice of cilantro or juice of anise or juice of wild parsnip in sour wine, and attach it to the location; and afterward treat the place with ointments until it is healed.
And cure him so that he may be healed.
Chapter LXXIV.
On the Incision of the Bladder in Accidental Cases Affecting the Belly.
Various kinds of abscesses occur in this area, such as gangrenous, lithic, ulcerative, hemorrhagic, phlegmonous, herpetic, fistulous, hemorrhoids, rectal abscesses, and other abscesses. And I have already discussed these illnesses and their kinds, the signs of them, and their treatments in detail.
And what I say in this treatise about abscesses that occur in the belly when they are among those that can be cured, and if you want to know how the operation is performed.
Then you must consider whether the pain of the abscess at its beginning is acute with percussion and phlegm and fever, and if there is redness and sensitivity in that area, do not perform an incision then, but treat it to aid maturation until the acuity of the symptoms subsides.
And now you should have the woman lie on a bench with two legs; let her recline on her back and place her feet at the part below the abdomen, and spread out her arms below her elbows, and bind them with bandages as is appropriate.
Follow the midwife with the right hand and administer the instrument with which to open the largest opening, the form of which will be made clear in the cases that will follow.
And when you want to administer this instrument, place it along the axis of the largest part of the woman's body, and ensure that what enters from the instrument into the largest opening does not exceed the size of the largest part and lead to injury. If the instrument is larger than the opening of the largest part, then at that time you should apply poultices to the tissue around the largest opening so that it becomes impossible to introduce any instrument into the largest opening.
And you should place the spiral that runs along the handle of the instrument above your hand, and have the minister hold the instrument while rotating the spiral so that it opens the largest opening.
And when the wound appears and is touched by the hand and feels hot and moist, then at that time you should dry it with a piece of linen.
And when the pus is evacuated, then you should place on the wound a piece of cloth submerged in olive oil or green oil, which has some astringent properties; and apply a bandage around the largest opening.
And place clean wool over the largest opening and on top of it, place linen soaked in water in which mallows have been boiled.
And it should be treated for about two days with the remedy that you consider appropriate until it is healed.
And in some cases, the largest opening and the wound should be washed with this so that it is cleansed with water and honey, and then with water in which rue or long-leaved artemisia has been boiled, and afterward return to the remedy.
And if the wound is inside the large cavity, then you must be prohibited from treating it with iron, but take care of that limb as we have said in the division.
Chapter LXXV.
To instruct midwives on how to treat male embryos in cases where there is an unnatural swelling as shown in the figure.
It is necessary that the midwife knows at the beginning the figure of normal childbirth by its signs. And it is when you see the woman push down and desire to smell the air, and she is encouraged by what is above her during labor; then you know that this birth is according to a natural figure, and the delivery is over the head of the child, and the second part is either suspended or hanging from the navel.
When you see those signs, then it is necessary to compress the abdomen so that the embryo descends gently, for when it delivers over its head, the second part will be delivered, and it should be cleaned of those superfluities with proper cleansing.
But if it is another kind of delivery, it is unnatural and not commendable, for when the embryo is delivered on its back and the body of the child is delivered in front of its head and behind its feet, with one hand or foot exposed first, or the head and a hand or foot turned to the side, or the belly facing forward, and easily turns around its neck, resembling the figures of those that are not commendable.
Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in all these matters and to guard against error and deception.
Here is the translation:
When the fetus is set upon the woman's head naturally, and it is strongly positioned on the woman and the birth is difficult in that place, and sometimes the strength of the womb has been weakened, then at this time one should cause her to expel it or allow her to have it, and evaporate the essence of fenugreek juice with warm oil.
And then insert the midwife's hand between those parts called the buttocks, and separate with the second finger, or dry it with her fingernail so that she can feel what is inside in terms of humidity. And press the woman's belly so that the fetus descends.
But if it does not descend, then at this time the woman should be anointed with powder of cyperus and powder of fenugreek with eggs.
And then command her, after the anointment, to be made to sneeze with appropriate conditions; and do this at her mouth and nose for one hour, because the fetus will be expelled shortly.
And if both sides of the fetus are expelled at the beginning, then it is necessary to reduce them to ease gradually. But if it does not obey the instrument, then place the woman on a cushion and raise her legs up, and then strike the cushion on the ground; and hold the woman so that she does not fall due to the impact.
And if the membranes are not returned and the fetus dies, then incise them and extract the remnants of the fetus or tie the body to your hand with a cloth and extract it gently, as it will be expelled.
When the fetus is cut on its sides, then you should push them up, and immediately turn the fetus slightly, and then even it out, and then take a piece of it and extend them little by little.
But when it is cut into the contents, then you command him to sneeze, and make that person sneeze under certain conditions, for it will be expelled if God wills it.
And if it is not expelled with what we have recommended, then you return the fetus little by little until you place it in its second natural position, for it will be expelled at that time with a simple incision.
And if it is prevented by everything we have recommended, then take musellage of hartshorn and dissolved gum, and triturate all in the mortar with good pounding, and then apply that mixture to the woman's cervix, at the bottom of her abdomen. And then make that person sit in warm water, until the hypochondria are reached.
And when the lower parts of him are cleansed, then perform the fumigation of myrtle and apply that to him. And when the sub-fumigation has been performed for one hour, then make him sit on a chair, and then make that person sneeze and expel the mouth of him, and take him away, and press the lower part of his abdomen gently, for the fetus will be expelled soon.
Deliver the fetus laterally with one of its parts. Attempt to reduce the hand of the fetus, but if you cannot reduce it, then elevate the woman and allow that to pass.
And if it cannot pass, then make her lie on her side, and strike the parts of the fetus with vigorous percussion, and then administer liniments which I use and recommend for soothing.
And if the childbirth has begun, then make her sit on a chair, and then study the reduction of the hand, and engage the fetus according to its natural position, and make the woman sneeze and command it [the fetus] to exert itself until it is completely delivered.
Deliver the fetus over the back with its parts and the fetal membrane at the side of its larger part. Let the midwife hold the fetus and gradually turn it little by little, and let that part be facilitated.
And when it is and how long it is soaked, then pause on the cooling of what we have recommended of oil and mucilage.
And then command him to squeeze it little by little, and when you have done this, now place that poultice on a cloth and command him to lean over the right side, and then command him to be restrained; and make him sneeze under certain conditions. The exit of the prepared fetus on the side.
When you begin the incision of the mother according to this method, consider it, and then you make the second cut with your fingernail so that it is evacuated of the humidity.
And if the fetus is suspended over the face and neck of the mother, then you make an incision at the abdomen, so that it is not restrained and dies.
And then push the fetus towards the internal parts until you pause at the second necessary point, and tell the woman to restrain herself for several times, and the issue will be expelled quickly if God so wills.
The exit of twins or multiple fetuses. Know that twins usually are born in separate births, but sometimes three or four may be born at once, though this is rare and uncommon; however, in some cases it is due to causes outside of nature, and not living.
And with these, whether they are multiple, make a second incision, and separate them by the cord, distinguish each one through the ligament at the navel of each. Sometimes they are expelled as one fetus would be in a natural quick manner, but sometimes they are expelled separately in an uncommendable way as we have mentioned.
And if any of them are difficult for the woman in childbirth and you come to those which we have said about the unnatural figures, then treat them as we have recounted.
And if the midwife is skilled and does what she should with ease and skill, and with delay when necessary, and acts according to every figure as it is prepared by the birth-giver for health.
A remembrance of what is formed in the womb from embryos and miscarriages.
Sometimes formations occur in the womb one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and sometimes more than ten, and you should now be convinced that a woman may miscarry at six months, and another at all formations, which cause was made by measurement of the glorious wise ones.
And all of this must be known by the midwife because it is easy to mistake one thing for another, and therefore she should know what needs to be done.
Chapter LXXVI.
On the extraction of the fetus when it is dead.
When you treat the dead fetus as we have said in the division of treatment and it is not successful, and you are forced to use surgery, then it is necessary for you to consider whether the woman is of sound constitution and is not subject to any of those accidents by which danger to her is feared.
Now it is necessary for the woman to be placed on her back on the bed with her buttocks raised and her head slightly lowered.
The minister should use a knife with two edges or tie it down firmly on the table so that the body does not move during the extraction.
And then moisten the mother's mouth with olive oil and honey, as well as mallow, fenugreek, and linseed.
And then the midwife anoints her hand with those oils and mallows, and then inserts it gently into the mother, and then searches with her hand for the location of the fetus.
And in these cases: then you consider whether the fetus is positioned to descend head first, and if so, place the hooks in its hands, or around its neck, or in its mouth, or on its palate, or under its chin, or at its clavicle, or near the ribs, or under the armpits.
But if the descent is foot first, then place the hooks in the heels, or in the middle of the back.
And it is necessary to hold the hook with the right hand, and place the curvature of it where the fingers of the left hand are, and insert the hand gently into the mother and place the hook in one of those places we have mentioned, until it reaches the obstruction.
And then hold and place another hook in position, or a third if necessary, so that there is an equal pull, and not just extension according to its straightness alone.
And it should be moistened at all times, so that the extraction of it is eased just as it is done during the removal of a tooth.
Place in the liquid that is between them so that the extension may be softened; and if any part of it is retained, then place that the midwife anoints some of her said hands with oil and interposes those skillfully and rolls back what is retained.
If the part of the fetus is presented incorrectly, then place the hooks between the places where it is more appropriate; and do this so that all of the fetus may be properly delivered.
But if one hand is presented before the other, and it is not possible to reduce that one by compression of it, then place a cloth wrapped around that one; and immediately extract that one so that all of it may be delivered, and incise it either at the joint of the hand or at the elbow.
And do the same with the other hand and both feet.
But if the head of the fetus is large, or compression occurs during its presentation, or it is in the tight fitting part of the water, then place between the said protruding spines and cut open the head to extract the water, or use an instrument called “alundat,” the form of which will be among the forms of other instruments in the chapter that follows this one.
And similarly do if the fetus has a large head by nature: then it is necessary to incise that with some instrument, or take that as we have said using an alundat; and immediately extract the bones with forceps.
And if the head is presented and is compressed behind the clavicle, then it should be cut open so that the moisture which is in the cheeks may be effused.
If it is not complicated and you do not wait too long, then cut into the head as soon as it is convenient for you.
And if the flanks of the abdomen are full of pus or are in a state of hydrops, then it is necessary for you to puncture that part which runs with the moisture that is there.
But if the fault is on the lesser vessels, then the attraction of it is weak and the direction of it towards the mouth of the artery is weak.
But if it is constricted in the abdomen and the thighs, then you must remove that piece of cloth with which you have wrapped around your hand, and cut into the abdomen and the thighs where the fluid runs.
But if the other members are stiff and turn the head, then insert your left hand; but if the mouth of the artery is open, then insert your hand into the chest, and search for the head, and pull it along with those mentioned to the mouth of the artery, and then insert about one or two inches, and pull it along with them.
And if the mouth of the artery is constricted by pus that has occurred due to illness, then it must not be compressed upon it; instead, you should administer an effusion of moist and fatty substances. And apply plasters; and follow with waters that soften and moisten.
And if the fault is on the side vessel, then if possible, it should be punctured; and what we have said about the living condition should be administered.
And if it cannot be done thus, then cut it into pieces and extract it.
And do not leave any cause for the second [operation].
And when you have completed the entire operation, now administer what we have said about the treatment after abscesses, of which there has been mention regarding the major ones.
And if bleeding occurs, then apply styptic waters and administer the other treatment.
And I have seen a woman in whose womb was a dead fetus, and next to it she was pregnant again, and beside the dead fetus another conception had taken place. It happened to one who had an abscess in the navel area for a long time; it became swollen inside with a pus-filled focus, and began to discharge pus.
And I was called to treat him, and treated him for a long time, but the condition did not improve.
Then I decided to apply some causes of strong attraction to him and extracted one bone from him, and after a few days, another bone was passed; and I was very surprised, as there were no bones in the abdomen.
And then I realized that they were from the bones of the dead fetus.
Then I examined the condition thoroughly and extracted several bones from her, which were located in various parts of her body. And in this manner over a long period, she expelled a small amount of pus.
This is not to be considered strange, but because in this there is science and assistance for what the surgeon does with his hand in administering treatment.
Of the forms of the instruments that are necessary to extract the fetus.
Form of a spiral used by the mother:
This is the form of a clamp with which the leaves are held equally, at the clamping point there are two spirals at the ends of two arms. However, this spiral should be finer than the string, and it should be made of reed or wood.
And the width of each arm should be two fingers, and the margin on each side should be one finger, and the length of each should be a palm and a half; and in the middle between the two arms there are two adjustments made from the same material as the arms, which are already fixed, their length being about half a palm more or less, and the width of each is two fingers, or slightly more.
And these two attachments should be inserted into the mother's mouth so that they are held when you turn the two prescribed spirals.
Another similar form, finer and more slender:
It should be made of reed or wood, resembling the form of forceps. However, at the end of each of these two attachments, as you see, the length of those attachments is one palm, and the width of each is two fingers.
And when you want to open one of them, then at that time you should cut the woman on her bed with her knees raised, exposing what is between her thighs. And then open your hand with the instrument as you would with scissors, equally according to the quantity that you want of the width of the mouth of the wound until the speculum does what you want.
The method of turning, which the ancients called:
Method of pushing with which the action is pushed forward:
Method of association with which the head is contained:
And it is similar to forceps, at the ends of which there are teeth, as you see. And sometimes it is made long like forceps according to this form, as you see, with teeth like those of a reed, with which it is incised and contained. Method of association for few:
Form of a hook having a spine:
Form of a hook having two spines:
Form of a speculum having two ends with which the head is engaged:
Form of two broad specula:
All those instruments are exercised, and when more varieties of them are multiplied and prepared by the artisans, it is easier for their operation and better for people according to their needs.
You should prepare those instruments which are necessary, for the need of them cannot be avoided.
Of the extraction of the second [tooth].
When the afterbirth is retained after childbirth, you should instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then cause her to sneeze by certain means. Place your hand over the mouth and nose of the patient, and if this causes it to come out, that is good.
And if that does not work, take a cloth and pierce it with a hole, placing it over the mouth of the mother along with herbs such as wormwood, rue, chamomile, Arabian saffron, cinnamon, and sage. All these herbs or some of them should be immersed in water in the cloth, and place that over the fire.
And then place a reed tube in the mouth of the mother, and hold it there until the vapor reaches the cavity of the mother.
And then cause her to sneeze as we have said, and the afterbirth will be expelled quickly.
But if this treatment delays and it does not come out, then you command the midwife to immerse her left hand in sesame oil or masticate almonds, and then insert that into the womb and gently pull out the afterbirth with it. If it is attached to the placenta of the mother, then insert her right hand as we have recommended, and when she has found the afterbirth, gently extract it little by little so that the mother does not fall due to violent traction. Take care that it is turned to the right and left with ease.
And if the mouth of the mother is obstructed, we have already recommended treatment through sneezing and medication of the wound with herbs.
But if it is not expelled by all the causes we have recommended, then do not exhaust yourself in repeated attempts of abstraction. Instead, ensure that what has been ejected from the mouth of the mother lies close to the woman's body, and subsequently treat it with abortion and tetrapharmacon; for this will cause it to be purged after a few days and thus dissolved and expelled.
But when it is purged, it rises to the head and to the stomach, causing illness; then it is necessary that sublimations and appropriate remedies be administered for this.
But some of the Ancients already used sublimation of nitre and dried figs.
Form of the instrument with which a woman is subjected to sublimation due to the retention of menstruation and the second condition:
It should be made of wood or ivory.
And the fine end should be placed in the vagina and the wider end above the fire, and the sublimation should be placed on the embers of the fire.
And keep that instrument inside until the sublimation is consumed, then repeat with another.
Of the treatment of the child's uncircumcised penis.
Many children are born and their penises are not circumcised, which must then be carefully opened and covered. Then it should be the midwife who pierces with her finger that foreskin; and if not, pierce it with a sharp scalpel, being careful not to cut the glans.
And then apply a poultice made of lint soaked in wine and oil; and afterwards, treat it with a dressing until it is healed.
But if you fear that it is obstructed, then insert a cannula for several days, and remove it when the child needs to urinate.
And if there is an obstruction of the penis due to the hardening of a wound or abscess; then it should be that this hardening be incised, and afterwards it should be treated as we have said regarding treatment and lead.
Of the treatment of fistulas that occur below.
Fistulas that occur in the lower region close to the body or near the buttocks or in the area between them are usually hard and thick.
And it is one fistula or multiple.
And as this hardness subsides and it discharges watery or slightly purulent white moisture, and sometimes these fistulas penetrate deeper.
And these penetrating ones are known by what is emitted from them through discharge and swelling; and sometimes the severity of the discharge indicates that they are very deep.
Of those fistulas, some extend into the space penetrating into the bladder, and into the shaft of the penis; and some penetrate into the joint of the thigh and into the root of the bone.
And in the one where it is known as a penetrating fistula into the anus and a non-penetrating fistula, you should insert your finger into the anus, and insert a fine probe of hair or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
But if there is tortuosity in that one, then insert the fine probe of lead or horsehair into it until you feel the probe or hair with your finger.
And if you do not feel anything of that and there is no process from the tract of any cause of evacuation or worms or gas, as we have said, then you know it is non-penetrating, and then proceed with the treatment.
And when the fistula is penetrating into the bladder or into the shaft of the penis, then the significance of that is that urine will come from there, and it prohibits this so that the place may be consolidated by medicine.
But if it is penetrating into the joint of the thigh or into the bone and causes pain in the circumference, then the sign of that is that the probe goes through there if there is no tortuosity within the bone, and causes pain in the circumference of the affected area; and you will have a persistent discharge from there; and that does not respond to medication, nor is it consolidated without treatment.
And in all those penetrating fistulas, there is no complete cure, and the treatment for these is the labor and persistence of skilled physicians, upon which depends their success.
In that which is not penetrating and not ancient, healing by iron is hoped for as I will tell you, and this that I say is good.
And it is that the patient should lie between your thighs with their back upwards and lift the flanks up, so that the contents are inclined towards the abdomen, and then insert a probe of lead or iron if there is tortuosity in the fistula, until you know where the probe passes.
And if the pain is around the anus, then you should insert your finger into the anus at that time.
And if you feel with your finger that the probe can easily penetrate, or what you feel between your finger and that sinus or flesh, then you know certainly that it is penetrating; and then do not work on that one, for there is no healing in that one, as we have said.
But some might say that it heals in some men slowly.
And for the treatment by which healing is hoped for involves you igniting a cautery subtly according to the size of the fistula, as has been described, and inserting that heated instrument into the fistula until it goes around the anus; and then repeat this two or three times until you know that all those inflamed tissues surrounding the fistula are tightened, so that they resemble the quill of a bird.
And then treat that with bandages wrapped in boiled cloth until all those tightened tissues grow and consolidate, and then treat it with medicines that promote tissue growth and consolidation. If it heals, good; but if not, then it will not heal at any time by other treatment.
And if the probe enters and does not penetrate inside; you say which is in the anus, and between that and the probe there is a thin layer of flesh or tissue, and sometimes the fistula is on what appears as the surface of the buttocks. Now dry the area from the beginning of the fistula, and you see drying around the probe, and it should reach to the place where the tip of the probe reaches, and through the probe it is freed and cured.
And then clean those fistulated tissues that resemble the hollow part of a bird's feather quill and do not tear any part of them for any reason.
But if blood flows when you are operating on those tissues, then the moment it happens during your procedure, immediately use a light instrument to cauterize with fire or with sharp medicine, because cauterizing with fire adjusts two good habits: one is the adjustment of those constricted tissues, and the other is the cessation of bleeding by removing excess moisture.
And then treat that with bandages wrapped in boiled cloth or soft lint until the area gets better, and afterwards cure the wound with hard flesh-producing remedies that generate and consolidate tissue.
And medicines that have astringent and drying properties; when they are restored, it is healed and you need not fear recurrence.
But if the fistula already penetrates inside the rectum and is long from the surface of the body, then insert your finger into the anus and examine it.

Regarding the suturing of hemorrhoids in which blood flows during the incision of those.
Hemorrhoids occur in two ways: either they appear around the anus like coal lumps, or they are soft and resemble grape clusters. And they can be small and large, and the blood flows from them constantly and is one type, and multiple, and some are outside the anus, and at its extremities.
However, those that are outside the anus are due to little moisture, from which yellowish water or a little blood flows continuously, and their color is like that of the skin.
And the treatment for those that are inside the anus is to instruct the patient to sit in such a way that the anus relaxes and the hemorrhoids become visible to you. Then you cover yourself and suspend with hooks or what you have those with your fingernail, and then cut them along their roots.
If the hooks do not hold in them because of their moisture and softness, then take some rough cloth or a cork or a flaxen pad, and extract them with these mentioned tools, and afterwards incise around them and sprinkle on them certain powders near the incision, so that they serve as cauterization; or cauterize them as is described in the chapter about cauterizing. And afterwards treat them with other treatments until they are healed.
And if the pus does not flow out, then incise the abscess with an incision that is small and wash it with the water in which it flows out easily when the abscess is squeezed.
But if the hemorrhoids are outside the anus, then their cause is easy to treat, and you should take them with your finger or hook, and incise them, and afterwards treat them as we have said until they are healed.
And for those who require suturing, proceed as follows: take silk wrapped around a needle and then extract the hemorrhoids at the top part, and make it penetrate with the needle on the other side of the incision, and wrap both ends of the thread underneath the part below the needle, and tie them horizontally; tighten the hemorrhoid firmly with the structure, and then knot the silk and extract the needle.
And do this for all of them, and leave one of them open and do not sew it up, so that the excess blood can flow out from it.
And then place on the wound a cloth soaked in rose oil or in cerate; and place that on the wound and instruct the patient to rest. And then place that inside the cavity; and when it is closed, treat those with applications or other treatment until it is healed.
And when they are old and do not respond to that medicine, you should then scrape those areas with the edge of a spatula or your fingernail until they are made wet and remove the pus from them, which prevents their consolidation; and then treat those areas until they are healed.
